It has a high mortality rate if ", 'alert_tag_id': None, 'dup_count': '0', 'dup_of': None, 'unique_string': '20220312.8701950', 'info_hash': None, 'submitted_by': '3404', 'reviewed': None, 'search_string_id': None, 'content': "MENINGITIS, MENINGOCOCCAL - MONGOLIA: YOUNG CHILDREN, ALERT, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Thu 10 Mar 2022 15:11 ULAT\r\nSource: Bol News [edited]\r\n<https://www.bolnews.com/latest/2022/03/mongolia-issues-warning-over-meningococcal-disease/>\r\n\r\n\r\nMongolia's Health Ministry declared an outbreak of the life-threatening meningococcal disease. Meningococcal infections have been reported among young children in the country recently, the ministry said on Thursday [10 Mar 2022], urging parents and guardians to take precautions to protect their children from the disease.\r\n\r\nThe disease is caused by bacteria named _Neisseria meningitidis_ and can cause infections in the linings of the brain or the blood, or both. It has a high mortality rate if untreated, but is vaccine-preventable. The common symptoms of the disease include sudden fever, vomiting, nausea, headache, a stiff neck, backache and increased sensitivity to light.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\n\n[_Neisseria meningitidis_, the cause of invasive meningococcal disease (IMD), infects only humans; there is no animal reservoir, and the organism dies quickly outside the human host. _N. meningitidis_, which colonizes the mucosal membranes of the nose and throat, is spread person to person by sharing respiratory and throat secretions (e.g., coughing or kissing). Close and prolonged contact with an infected person or carrier facilitates the spread of the disease. The average incubation period is 4 days but can range between 2 and 10 days.\r\n\r\nPeople at increased risk of IMD include household members and roommates of a patient with IMD, and anyone with direct contact with the patient's oral secretions, such as a boyfriend or girlfriend. These close contacts should receive antibiotics to help prevent them from getting the disease.\r\n\r\nMeningococcal meningitis occurs most frequently in the elderly, infants, and teenagers and young adults, especially if living in group settings, such as dormitories, boarding schools and military bases. Certain rare medical conditions and medications increase the risk for IMD, including complement component deficiencies, functional or anatomic asplenia, HIV/AIDS, and complement inhibitor medications, e.g., eculizumab (Soliris) and ravulizumab (Ultomiris).\r\n\r\nWe are not told in the news report above the demographic characteristics or underlying medical conditions of the patients in the outbreak of IMD in Mongolia, other than they were young children. Nor are we told the number of cases, the timeline over which the cases occurred, or the geographic distribution of the cases.\r\n\r\nMeningococci are classified into serogroups based on the antigenic specificity of their polysaccharide capsule. Although there are at least 13 _N. meningitidis_ serogroups, 6 serogroups (A, B, C, X, W, and Y) cause almost all IMD globally. Immunity following the use of a meningococcal capsular polysaccharide vaccine is specific for the type of capsular polysaccharide that the vaccine contains, with no cross-protection against infection due to other meningococcal polysaccharide groups. Some vaccines contain capsular polysaccharides (A, C, Y, W), conjugated to a protein, e.g., the MenC and the quadrivalent MenACWY vaccines. Conjugate vaccines immunize infants, reduce the carriage of meningococci in the throat and thus its transmission, as well as confer a more sustained immune response, and, therefore, longer-term protection than vaccines that contain polysaccharide alone. Serogroup B (MenB) vaccines are based upon meningococcal B protein antigens because group B capsular polysaccharide is poorly immunogenic in humans and may stimulate autoantibodies.\r\n\r\nSome countries, such as in the UK, include meningococcal vaccines in their routine childhood vaccine schedule (<https://vk.ovg.ox.ac.uk/vk/uk-schedule>). We are not told in the news report above if Mongolia's routine childhood vaccine schedule includes a meningococcal vaccine, the vaccine status of the infected children, or the meningococcal serogroup(s) of the outbreak strain(s).\r\n\r\nMore information on this outbreak from knowledgeable sources would be appreciated. - Meningococcal infections have been reported among young children in the country recently, the ministry said on Thursday [10 Mar 2022], urging parents and guardians to take precautions to protect their children from the disease.<br /><br />The disease is caused by bacteria named _Neisseria meningitidis_ and can cause infections in the linings of the brain or the blood, or both. It has a high mortality rate if untreated, but is vaccine-preventable. The common symptoms of the disease include sudden fever, vomiting, nausea, headache, a stiff neck, backache and increased sensitivity to light.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED from HealthMap Alerts<br /><br />[_Neisseria meningitidis_, the cause of invasive meningococcal disease (IMD), infects only humans; there is no animal reservoir, and the organism dies quickly outside the human host. _N. meningitidis_, which colonizes the mucosal membranes of the nose and throat, is spread person to person by sharing respiratory and throat secretions (e.g., coughing or kissing). Close and prolonged contact with an infected person or carrier facilitates the spread of the disease. The average incubation period is 4 days but can range between 2 and 10 days.<br /><br />People at increased risk of IMD include household members and roommates of a patient with IMD, and anyone with direct contact with the patient\'s oral secretions, such as a boyfriend or girlfriend. These close contacts should receive antibiotics to help prevent them from getting the disease.<br /><br />Meningococcal meningitis occurs most frequently in the elderly, infants, and teenagers and young adults, especially if living in group settings, such as dormitories, boarding schools and military bases. Certain rare medical conditions and medications increase the risk for IMD, including complement component deficiencies, functional or anatomic asplenia, HIV/AIDS, and complement inhibitor medications, e.g., eculizumab (Soliris) and ravulizumab (Ultomiris).<br /><br />We are not told in the news report above the demographic characteristics or underlying medical conditions of the patients in the outbreak of IMD in Mongolia, other than they were young children. Nor are we told the number of cases, the timeline over which the cases occurred, or the geographic distribution of the cases.<br /><br />Meningococci are classified into serogroups based on the antigenic specificity of their polysaccharide capsule. Although there are at least 13 _N. meningitidis_ serogroups, 6 serogroups (A, B, C, X, W, and Y) cause almost all IMD globally. Immunity following the use of a meningococcal capsular polysaccharide vaccine is specific for the type of capsular polysaccharide that the vaccine contains, with no cross-protection against infection due to other meningococcal polysaccharide groups. Some vaccines contain capsular polysaccharides (A, C, Y, W), conjugated to a protein, e.g., the MenC and the quadrivalent MenACWY vaccines. Conjugate vaccines immunize infants, reduce the carriage of meningococci in the throat and thus its transmission, as well as confer a more sustained immune response, and, therefore, longer-term protection than vaccines that contain polysaccharide alone. Serogroup B (MenB) vaccines are based upon meningococcal B protein antigens because group B capsular polysaccharide is poorly immunogenic in humans and may stimulate autoantibodies.<br /><br />Some countries, such as in the UK, include meningococcal vaccines in their routine childhood vaccine schedule (<a href="https://vk.ovg.ox.ac.uk/vk/uk-schedule" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://vk.ovg.ox.ac.uk/vk/uk-schedule</a>). 'submitted_by': '3234', 'reviewed': None, 'search_string_id': None, 'content': 'FOOT & MOUTH DISEASE - PALESTINIAN AUTHORITY: (WEST BANK, GAZA) SEROTYPE O, GENOTYPES, SPREAD, CONTROL\n******************************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Fri 11 Mar 2022 \r\nSource: Xinhua News Agency [in Arabic, machine trans., abridged, edited] \r\n<http://arabic.news.cn/2022-03/11/c_1310508955.htm>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe Palestinian Minister of Agriculture, Riyad Al-Atari, announced the closure of livestock markets in the West Bank for a period of one month due to the spread of foot-and-mouth disease (FMD). \r\n\r\nAl-Atari told reporters in Ramallah that the disease has spread widely, and it is a cross-border disease, noting that the measure is preventive, as the focus is on monitoring the movement of animals. \r\n\r\nAl-Atari added that his ministry had provided 400 000 vaccine doses in February [2022], as about 70% of sheep and goats and 95% of cows were vaccinated, pointing out that the ministry continues to vaccinate despite the shortage of vaccines globally. \r\n\r\nHe pointed out that the Ministry of Agriculture recommended the necessity of stopping livestock markets to prevent mixing of animals and transmission of infection, stressing that matters are under control, as there is a crisis management team in order to mitigate losses. \r\n\r\nAl-Atari explained that the disease is not transmitted to humans and there is no danger in eating infected sheep products, and it is expected that its spread will decrease after taking various measures to limit its transmission. \r\n\r\nHe pointed out that the ministry has sent 10 000 vaccine doses to the Gaza Strip in order to protect livestock, pointing out that there is a protocol for imported livestock to remain quarantined for a specific period in agreement with importers, expecting that the disease will begin to decline in the middle of April [2022]. \r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED-MENA\n\n[The FMDV serotype O that has been causing the above described epizootic in the West Bank district of the Palestinian Authority (P.A.) since 12 Dec 2021, has been genotyped as FMDV O, topotype ME-SA, lineage PanAsia 2, sublineage ANT-10. A similar strain has been circulating in Jordan (starting early November 2021). Their similarity has been demonstrated by their identical sequencing results which have become available on the Jordan report section in the website of the world reference laboratory for FMD, Pirbright, at <https://www.wrlfmd.org/sites/world/files/quick_media/WRLMEG-2021-00020-PAT-GTR-O-O_001.pdf>.\r\n\r\nThe genotyping results of (one) sample from the West Bank are available in a separate P.A.T. report, at <https://www.wrlfmd.org/sites/world/files/quick_media/WRLMEG-2021-00022-JOR-GTR-O-O_001.pdf>.\r\n\r\nThe said report includes also the genotyping results of a sample collected in a separate district of the P.A., namely the Gaza strip. The event there was reported to the OIE by the P.A. on 24 Dec 2021 (Archive number 20211224.8700454). Its details, as presented on the WRLFMD are: \r\nVirus sample name: 437694-0257/PAT/2021; \r\nSender reference: Gaza_437694-0257; \r\nLocation of origin: Northern part of the Gaza Strip;\r\nDate of collection: 12/2021; \r\nHost species: cattle. \r\nGenotyping results: FMDV O, topotype EA-3. This strain was found closely related to Egyptian strains (see the table titled "Most Closely Related Sequences" and the dendogram). Notably, the same topotype was reported from Gaza in February 2019 (Archive number 20190216.6320472).\r\n\r\nFMD has been reported from neighboring Israel since early February 2022. So far, 3 villages have been reportedly affected. The infected animals include dairy cattle, fattening calves and sheep. Their vaccination status is yet to be clarified. The virus was sequenced and genotyped by the Kimron Veterinary Institute as FMDV-O, PanAsia 2, ANT-10. \r\n\r\nIn summary, currently FMDV-O PanAsia-2 ANT-10 is circulating in Jordan, the West Bank (P.A.) and Israel while FMD-O EA-3 (an East African strain) has been circulating in the Gaza strip (P.A.). An update of the situation there will be useful.\r\n\r\nVaccine matching results for both strains are anticipated. - Mod.AS\n\nProMED map:\nPalestinian Authority: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701947,92>]\n\n[See Also:\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel: (HZ) cattle, goat, st O, OIE 20210107.8079606\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Syria: (LA) goat, spread, RFI 20210422.8320257\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Syria: (HA) livestock, spread, Iraq susp, RFI 20210216.8194894\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Lebanon: (NA) cattle, spread, RFI 20210219.8201498\r\n2019\r\n----\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Palestinian Auth (02): (WE) sheep, goats, st pending, OIE 20190403.6400967\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Palestinian Auth: (WE) sheep, 2018, st O, tt EA-3 20190216.6320472\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (04): (HA) cattle, st O, spread, OIE 20190807.6610873\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (03): (HA) cattle, gt Foot) 20190524.6486015\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (02): (HA) cattle, st. pending, OIE, RFI 20190510.6462227\r\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel: (HZ) cattle, st. href="http://arabic.news.cn/2022-03/11/c_1310508955.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://arabic.news.cn/2022-03/11/c_1310508955.htm</a><br /><br /><br />The Palestinian Minister of Agriculture, Riyad Al-Atari, announced the closure of livestock markets in the West Bank for a period of one month due to the spread of foot-and-mouth disease (FMD). <br /><br />Al-Atari told reporters in Ramallah that the disease has spread widely, and it is a cross-border disease, noting that the measure is preventive, as the focus is on monitoring the movement of animals. <br /><br />Al-Atari added that his ministry had provided 400 000 vaccine doses in February [2022], as about 70% of sheep and goats and 95% of cows were vaccinated, pointing out that the ministry continues to vaccinate despite the shortage of vaccines globally. <br /><br />He pointed out that the Ministry of Agriculture recommended the necessity of stopping livestock markets to prevent mixing of animals and transmission of infection, stressing that matters are under control, as there is a crisis management team in order to mitigate losses. <br /><br />Al-Atari explained that the disease is not transmitted to humans and there is no danger in eating infected sheep products, and it is expected that its spread will decrease after taking various measures to limit its transmission. <br /><br />He pointed out that the ministry has sent 10 000 vaccine doses to the Gaza Strip in order to protect livestock, pointing out that there is a protocol for imported livestock to remain quarantined for a specific period in agreement with importers, expecting that the disease will begin to decline in the middle of April [2022]. <br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED-MENA<br /><br />[The FMDV serotype O that has been causing the above described epizootic in the West Bank district of the Palestinian Authority (P.A.) since 12 Dec 2021, has been genotyped as FMDV O, topotype ME-SA, lineage PanAsia 2, sublineage ANT-10. A similar strain has been circulating in Jordan (starting early November 2021). Their similarity has been demonstrated by their identical sequencing results which have become available on the Jordan report section in the website of the world reference laboratory for FMD, Pirbright, at <a href="https://www.wrlfmd.org/sites/world/files/quick_media/WRLMEG-2021-00020-PAT-GTR-O-O_001.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.wrlfmd.org/sites/world/files/quick_media/WRLMEG-2021-00020-PAT-GTR-O-O_001.pdf</a>.<br /><br />The genotyping results of (one) sample from the West Bank are available in a separate P.A.T. report, at <a href="https://www.wrlfmd.org/sites/world/files/quick_media/WRLMEG-2021-00022-JOR-GTR-O-O_001.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.wrlfmd.org/sites/world/files/quick_media/WRLMEG-2021-00022-JOR-GTR-O-O_001.pdf</a>.<br /><br />The said report includes also the genotyping results of a sample collected in a separate district of the P.A., namely the Gaza strip. The event there was reported to the OIE by the P.A. on 24 Dec 2021 (Archive number <a href="javascript:;" onclick="window.open(\'https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=20211224.8700454\');">20211224.8700454</a>). This strain was found closely related to Egyptian strains (see the table titled "Most Closely Related Sequences" and the dendogram). Notably, the same topotype was reported from Gaza in February 2019 (Archive number <a href="javascript:;" onclick="window.open(\'https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=20190216.6320472\');">20190216.6320472</a>).<br /><br />FMD has been reported from neighboring Israel since early February 2022. So far, 3 villages have been reportedly affected. The infected animals include dairy cattle, fattening calves and sheep. Their vaccination status is yet to be clarified. The virus was sequenced and genotyped by the Kimron Veterinary Institute as FMDV-O, PanAsia 2, ANT-10. <br /><br />In summary, currently FMDV-O PanAsia-2 ANT-10 is circulating in Jordan, the West Bank (P.A.) and Israel while FMD-O EA-3 (an East African strain) has been circulating in the Gaza strip (P.A.). An update of the situation there will be useful.<br /><br />Vaccine matching results for both strains are anticipated. - Mod.AS<br /><br />ProMED map:<br />Palestinian Authority: <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701947,92" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701947,92</a>] <h2>See Also</h2>\nFoot & mouth disease - Sex and habitat drive hantavirus prevalence in marsh rice rat populations impacted by the Deepwater Horizon oil spill. Ecosphere. 2022; 13(2): e3929; <https://doi.org/10.1002/ecs2.3929>\r\n\r\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\n\r\nAbstract\r\n--------\r\nBayou orthohantavirus (BAYV) is one of several hantaviruses in the United States that cause hantavirus pulmonary syndrome in humans. Its host reservoir, the marsh rice rat (_Oryzomys palustris_), inhabits coastal saltmarshes of Louisiana, a region extensively impacted by anthropogenic disturbances, such as the 2010 Deepwater Horizon (DWH) oil spill. The oil spill presents an opportunity to investigate how a large-scale ecological disturbance can influence the hantavirus host-pathogen dynamic by examining BAYV presence in its reservoir host species in areas with different oiling histories. Here, we: (1) quantify BAYV prevalence in the rice rat in coastal saltmarshes of Louisiana; (2) assess whether prevalence is driven by rice rat demographics, seasonality, or association with habitat characteristics; and (3) determine whether these factors differ by marsh oiling history. We collected mark-recapture data and blood and tissue samples over 5 years (2013-2017) at oiled, unoiled, and reference sites. Testing of the samples for BAYV revealed an antibody and RNA prevalence of 13.7%. Logistic regression analysis found that prevalence varied seasonally and interannually, and in July 2016 reached 30.8%. Sex (male) and increasing cover of _Sporobolus alterniflorus_ and open water compared to _Juncus roemerianus_ and bare ground were the strongest predictors of hantavirus prevalence. Abundance estimates derived from Huggins closed-capture models were greatest at oiled sites, but oiling treatment had no residual influence on BAYV prevalence, and abundance and prevalence were not correlated. This study supports the hypothesis that habitat is a main driver of hantavirus prevalence in the host and implies that continued and future disturbances in the region will likely impact the rice rat-BAYV dynamic by altering plant communities and landscape structure.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMahmoud Orabi\r\n<ahstandards@gmail.com>\n\n[ProMED thanks Mahmoud Orabi for submitting this report.\r\n\r\nAlthough cases of Bayou hantavirus causing human hantavirus cardiopulmonary syndrome (HPS) have occurred infrequently, they have been diagnosed in eastern Texas and Louisiana. The above report underscores the importance of the relationship of habitat of the rodent reservoir host, the marsh rice rat (_Oryzomys palustris_), and prevalence of Bayou hantavirus. Human or naturally caused habitat changes can, in turn, affect BAY virus prevalence. People entering into these wetland areas of high BAY virus prevalence are at risk of infection.\r\n\r\nReferences\r\n----------\r\nKsiazek TG, Nichol ST, Mills JN, et al. Isolation, genetic diversity, and geographic distribution of Bayou virus (Bunyaviridae: Hantavirus). Am J Trop Med Hygiene. 1997; 57(4): 445-8; <https://doi.org/10.4269/ajtmh.1997.57.445>\r\nTorrez-Martinez N, Bharadwaj M, Goade D, et al. Bayou virus-associated hantavirus pulmonary syndrome in Eastern Texas: identification of the rice rat, _Oryzomys palustris_, as reservoir host. Emerg Infect Dis. 1998; 4(1): 105-11; <https://doi.org/10.3201/eid0401.980115>\r\n- Mod.TY\n\nProMED map:\nLouisiana, United States: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701946,221>]\n\n[See Also:\n2004\r\n----\r\nHantavirus pulmonary syndrome update 2004 - the Americas (05) 20041125.3154]\n.................................................ml/ty/rd/jh'}, 'post': '<span class="printable"><p><img src="https://promedmail.org/wp-content/plugins/promed-latest-post/assets/images/printer.gif"/><a href="javascript:;" onclick="window.open(\'https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8701946\');"> View printable version</a> &nbsp; The information was released by the municipality on Tuesday [22 Feb 2022]. In December of last year [2021], the City Hall also carried out the vaccine blockade in the region of Moreeiras, for the same reason.\r\n\r\nThe cattle testing positive for rabies was located in the community of Basilio, in the district of Areado, which is about 40 km [25 mi] from the city. The mobilization, which is called anti-rabies blockade, involved domestic animals within a 5 km [3 mi] radius of the place.\r\n\r\nIn all, 326 dogs and 111 cats were vaccinated. Part of them already received the vaccine in 2021, but were revaccinated according to the guidance of the competent state bodies. The city took the opportunity to guide the population on the importance of immunizing animals and ways of transmitting and preventing the disease.\r\n\r\n"It is important to highlight that the vaccination of cattle and horses against rabies has become mandatory, on behalf of the owner of the animals, although the declaration to the Mineiro de Agropecuária Institute (IMA) is not mandatory. Anyway, this will help a lot to avoid occurrences like this", explains the director of Health Surveillance in the city, Lílian Marinho.\r\n\r\nThe professional also says the vaccination blockade of dogs and cats is a way to eliminate one of the cycles of transmission of the disease, since, if an animal was detected with rabies, it is because there are bats infected with the virus in the region and that could infect other mammals.\r\n\r\nAccording to the Patos de Minas City Hall, rabies is transmitted by bats feeding on blood, the so-called hematophagous bats. [This is likely the species more commonly known as the vampire bat. - Mod.TG]\r\n\r\nWith the virus present in saliva, it transmits the disease by sucking or licking blood from mammals, such as horses, cattle, dogs and cats. Therefore, domestic animals are the main transmission agents for humans. [If this is the vampire bat, it most likely makes a tiny razor-like cut in the skin and then licks the blood from the wound. These bats are known to feed on cattle and horses, especially at night. - Mod.TG]\r\n\r\n"Rabies is a serious disease, with a lethality rate close to 100%. For more information, contact the Zoonosis Control Center by phone at (34) 3822-9624 (7am to 6pm)", concludes the municipality.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMahmoud Orabi\r\n<ahsandards@gmail.com>\r\n\r\n******\r\n[2] USA: California, bat, human exposure\r\nDate: Wed 2 Mar 2022\r\nSource: My News LA [edited]\r\n<https://mynewsla.com/orange-county/2022/03/02/boys-possibly-exposed-to-rabies-infected-bat-in-corona/>\r\n\r\n\r\nTwo boys who possibly handled a rabies-infected bat in Corona could suffer health complications, prompting Riverside County officials Wednesday [2 Mar 2022] to urge their parents to have the children tested.\r\n \r\nThe youths, described only as 11- to 12-year-olds on bicycles, may have picked up the rabid bat Monday afternoon [28 Feb 2022] before it died, according to the Department of Public Health.\r\n \r\nHealth officials said a man who later retrieved the creature and turned it over to health officials said he spotted the youths, who appeared to touch the bat. It was lying in the parking area of an industrial park at 301 Lincoln Ave., officials said.\r\n\r\n"It is important these children be seen by a health care provider because of the potential for a serious health issue," county Public Health Officer Dr. Geoffrey Leung said.\r\n \r\nThe bat was confirmed to have been a carrier of rabies following tests at a county lab, he said.\r\n \r\nRabies impacts the central nervous system and is transmitted through saliva of a wild animal. Humans can be exposed if they\'re bitten, or if the saliva otherwise enters a break in a person\'s skin, according to the California Department of Public Health.\r\n \r\nA rabies vaccine is available, but if it is not administered in time, "there is no effective treatment, and the infected person will likely die within a few days," CDPH said.\r\n \r\nAnyone with concerns about exposure risks was encouraged to contact the county health department at 951-358-5107.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED HealthMap Alerts\r\n\r\n******\r\n[3] USA: Florida (Polk County) bat, dog\r\nDate: Thu 3 Mar 2022\r\nSource: WFTV \r\n<https://bit.ly/3KBFQaq>\r\n\r\n\r\nAnimal Control officials have confirmed the 1st case of rabies this year [2022] in Polk County.\r\n \r\nOfficials said a bat had tested positive for the deadly virus on [3 Mar 2022].\r\n \r\nAccording to the Polk County Sheriff\'s Office Animal Control Section, a family dog in the Lake Mirror area of Winter Haven was found with a live bat in its mouth on [1 Mar 2022].\r\n \r\nThe family contacted Animal Control which then sent the bat to a Tampa lab for testing.\r\n\r\nOfficials say the dog was current on its rabies vaccination, but will still need to be quarantined to make sure it is not infected. [Although the dog is current on its rabies vaccination, it is recommended by the rabies compendium to revaccinate immediately and then placed under a 45-day quarantine, instead of a 4-month quarantine. The compendium implies this quarantine may be a home quarantine provided certain qualifications are met. - Mod.TG] \r\n \r\nPolk County had 5 confirmed cases of rabies in 2021, and 2 in 2020.\r\n \r\nOfficials warn residents if a wild mammal is acting aggressive or appears sick to stay away and contact Animal Control immediately.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Matt Reeser]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n \r\n******\r\n[4] USA: Florida (Hillsborough County) cat, human exposure\r\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022\r\nSource: Bay News 9 [edited]\r\n<https://www.baynews9.com/fl/tampa/news/2022/03/08/rabies-alert-east-bank-drive-tampa>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe Florida Department of Health in Hillsborough County has issued a rabies alert for the area surrounding East Bank Drive in the northeast Tampa area after a cat tested positive for rabies Monday [7 Mar 2022].\r\n\r\nThe cat was a black domestic short-haired stray cat. One person was confirmed to have been exposed and has begun rabies post-exposure vaccinations.\r\n \r\nThis rabies alert is for 60 days and includes the area bounded by Puritan Road on the north, 56th Street to the east, East Sligh Avenue to the south and the Hillsborough River to the west.\r\n\r\nThis is the 2nd rabies alert the health department issued in Hillsborough County Tuesday [8 Mar 2022].\r\n\r\nThe county also issued an alert for Glen Harwell Road in Plant City after a white and gray stray cat tested positive for rabies. Two people were confirmed exposed and have begun post-rabies vaccinations.\r\n\r\nThis alert is for 60 days as well and includes the area bordered by Interstate 4 to the north, Branch Forbes Road to the east, U.S. 92 to the south and Bethlehem Road to the west.\r\n \r\nAnyone who has been bitten, scratched or exposed to the saliva of these cats is asked to report the exposure to DOH-Hillsborough at 813-307-8059.\r\n\r\nThe Department of Health (DOH) is reminding residents to stay away from wild animals and make sure all their pets are vaccinated and do not roam free.\r\n \r\nRabies is a disease of the nervous system and is fatal to warm-blooded animals and humans. The only treatment for human exposure to rabies is rabies-specific immune globulin and rabies immunizations [Post Exposure Prophylaxis or PEP].\r\n\r\nPeople who have been bitten or scratched by wild or domestic animals should seek medical attention right away.\r\n\r\n[Byline: D\'Ann Lawrence]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\n\n[In the 1st article from Brazil, the bat in question is most likely what is commonly known as the vampire bat. It is known for feeding on cattle and a host of other animals. There are 3 species of hematophagous bats in the Neotropical region, one of which -- _Desmodus rotundus_ -- is a well-known reservoir of rabies. This species feeds on a wide range of hosts, including humans, although it will preferentially feed on large livestock such as cattle and horses. For a picture of _D. rotundus_ go to <https://www.inaturalist.org/taxa/41168-Desmodus-rotundus/browse_photos>.\r\n\r\nRabies is a viral disease affecting the central nervous system of its victim, regardless of whether it is a human victim or an animal victim. This virus has no mercy and without treatment, its victim will die. \r\n\r\nWhile we recognize rabies prevention in the form of rabies vaccination for our animals, and for some high risk human beings, such as veterinarians and persons involved in animal control, it is not a wide spread practice to vaccinate human beings against rabies. Therefore, when an individual is exposed to this lethal virus, post exposure prophylaxis (PEP) must be administered. This is a series of human immunoglobulin and PEP to prevent rabies in human beings but it must be started very soon after the exposure. In the case of bats in a room where an individual was sleeping, PEP is recommended as bats can bite a sleeping individual and not awaken them.\r\n\r\nIf you have pets, including horses and other farm animals, it is the wise, prudent move to vaccinate them against rabies. It protects your pets and yourself. Even if you do not know if there has been exposure to your animal, you are more likely to be protected. - Mod.TG\n\nProMED maps:\nBrazil: USA: Florida (Hillsborough County) cat, human exposure<br /><br />******<br />[1] Brazil: (Alto Paranaíba) cattle <br />Date: Tue 22 Feb 2022<br />Source: Otempo [in Portuguese, machine trans., edited]<br /><a href="https://www.otempo.com.br/cidades/caso-de-raiva-em-bovino-de-patos-de-minas-mobiliza-prefeitura-1.2619328" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.otempo.com.br/cidades/caso-de-raiva-em-bovino-de-patos-de-minas-mobiliza-prefeitura-1.2619328</a><br /><br /><br />After the notification of a positive case of rabies in a bovine in 1 of its districts, the Health Surveillance of the Municipality of Patos de Minas, in Alto Paranaíba, was mobilized to vaccinate dogs and cats in the region where the sick animal was found. The information was released by the municipality on Tuesday [22 Feb 2022]. In December of last year [2021], the City Hall also carried out the vaccine blockade in the region of Moreeiras, for the same reason.<br /><br />The cattle testing positive for rabies was located in the community of Basilio, in the district of Areado, which is about 40 km [25 mi] from the city. The mobilization, which is called anti-rabies blockade, involved domestic animals within a 5 km [3 mi] radius of the place.<br /><br />In all, 326 dogs and 111 cats were vaccinated. Part of them already received the vaccine in 2021, but were revaccinated according to the guidance of the competent state bodies. The city took the opportunity to guide the population on the importance of immunizing animals and ways of transmitting and preventing the disease.<br /><br />"It is important to highlight that the vaccination of cattle and horses against rabies has become mandatory, on behalf of the owner of the animals, although the declaration to the Mineiro de Agropecuária Institute (IMA) is not mandatory. Anyway, this will help a lot to avoid occurrences like this", explains the director of Health Surveillance in the city, Lílian Marinho.<br /><br />The professional also says the vaccination blockade of dogs and cats is a way to eliminate one of the cycles of transmission of the disease, since, if an animal was detected with rabies, it is because there are bats infected with the virus in the region and that could infect other mammals.<br /><br />According to the Patos de Minas City Hall, rabies is transmitted by bats feeding on blood, the so-called hematophagous bats. [This is likely the species more commonly known as the vampire bat. - Mod.TG]<br /><br />With the virus present in saliva, it transmits the disease by sucking or licking blood from mammals, such as horses, cattle, dogs and cats. Therefore, domestic animals are the main transmission agents for humans. [If this is the vampire bat, it most likely makes a tiny razor-like cut in the skin and then licks the blood from the wound. These bats are known to feed on cattle and horses, especially at night. - Mod.TG]<br /><br />"Rabies is a serious disease, with a lethality rate close to 100%. For more information, contact the Zoonosis Control Center by phone at (34) 3822-9624 (7am to 6pm)", concludes the municipality.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mahmoud Orabi<br />&lt;ahsandards@gmail.com><br /><br />******<br />[2] USA: California, bat, human exposure<br />Date: Wed 2 Mar 2022<br />Source: My News LA [edited]<br /><a href="https://mynewsla.com/orange-county/2022/03/02/boys-possibly-exposed-to-rabies-infected-bat-in-corona/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://mynewsla.com/orange-county/2022/03/02/boys-possibly-exposed-to-rabies-infected-bat-in-corona/</a><br /><br /><br />Two boys who possibly handled a rabies-infected bat in Corona could suffer health complications, prompting Riverside County officials Wednesday [2 Mar 2022] to urge their parents to have the children tested.<br /> <br />The youths, described only as 11- to 12-year-olds on bicycles, may have picked up the rabid bat Monday afternoon [28 Feb 2022] before it died, according to the Department of Public Health.<br /> <br />Health officials said a man who later retrieved the creature and turned it over to health officials said he spotted the youths, who appeared to touch the bat. It was lying in the parking area of an industrial park at 301 Lincoln Ave., officials said.<br /><br />"It is important these children be seen by a health care provider because of the potential for a serious health issue," county Public Health Officer Dr. Geoffrey Leung said.<br /> <br />The bat was confirmed to have been a carrier of rabies following tests at a county lab, he said.<br /> <br />Rabies impacts the central nervous system and is transmitted through saliva of a wild animal. Humans can be exposed if they\'re bitten, or if the saliva otherwise enters a break in a person\'s skin, according to the California Department of Public Health.<br /> <br />A rabies vaccine is available, but if it is not administered in time, "there is no effective treatment, and the infected person will likely die within a few days," CDPH said.<br /> <br />Anyone with concerns about exposure risks was encouraged to contact the county health department at 951-358-5107.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED HealthMap Alerts<br /><br />******<br />[3] USA: Florida (Polk County) bat, dog<br />Date: Thu 3 Mar 2022<br />Source: WFTV <br /><a href="https://bit.ly/3KBFQaq" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://bit.ly/3KBFQaq</a><br /><br /><br />Animal Control officials have confirmed the 1st case of rabies this year [2022] in Polk County.<br /> <br />Officials said a bat had tested positive for the deadly virus on [3 Mar 2022].<br /> <br />According to the Polk County Sheriff\'s Office Animal Control Section, a family dog in the Lake Mirror area of Winter Haven was found with a live bat in its mouth on [1 Mar 2022].<br /> <br />The family contacted Animal Control which then sent the bat to a Tampa lab for testing.<br /><br />Officials say the dog was current on its rabies vaccination, but will still need to be quarantined to make sure it is not infected. It is known for feeding on cattle and a host of other animals. There are 3 species of hematophagous bats in the Neotropical region, one of which -- _Desmodus rotundus_ -- is a well-known reservoir of rabies. This species feeds on a wide range of hosts, including humans, although it will preferentially feed on large livestock such as cattle and horses. For a picture of _D. rotundus_ go to <a href="https://www.inaturalist.org/taxa/41168-Desmodus-rotundus/browse_photos" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.inaturalist.org/taxa/41168-Desmodus-rotundus/browse_photos</a>.<br /><br />Rabies is a viral disease affecting the central nervous system of its victim, regardless of whether it is a human victim or an animal victim. This virus has no mercy and without treatment, its victim will die. <br /><br />While we recognize rabies prevention in the form of rabies vaccination for our animals, and for some high risk human beings, such as veterinarians and persons involved in animal control, it is not a wide spread practice to vaccinate human beings against rabies. Therefore, when an individual is exposed to this lethal virus, post exposure prophylaxis (PEP) must be administered. This is a series of human immunoglobulin and PEP to prevent rabies in human beings but it must be started very soon after the exposure. In the case of bats in a room where an individual was sleeping, PEP is recommended as bats can bite a sleeping individual and not awaken them.<br /><br />If you have pets, including horses and other farm animals, it is the wise, prudent move to vaccinate them against rabies. It protects your pets and yourself. Even if you do not know if there has been exposure to your animal, you are more likely to be protected. - Mod.TG<br /><br />ProMED maps:<br />Brazil: <a GLOBAL\n****************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nIn this update:\r\n[1] CIDRAP News\r\n[A] COVID case count\r\n[B] Hawaii: mask mandate\r\n[2] USA: deaths\r\n[3] CIDRAP News\r\n[A] UK: BA.2\r\n[B] USA: coronavirus package\r\n[4] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 10 Mar 2022)\r\n[5] Global update: Worldometer accessed 10 Mar 2022 22:32 EST (GMT-5)\r\n\r\n******\r\n[1] CIDRAP News\r\n[A] COVID case count\r\nDate: Wed 9 Mar 2022\r\nSource: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]\r\n<https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/global-drop-covid-19-continues-cases-still-high>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe world\'s COVID-19 cases declined last week for the 5th week in a row, but hotspots remain in a handful of countries, especially in Asia, the World Health Organization (WHO) said in its latest weekly update.\r\n\r\nCases declined 5% last week compared to the week before, marking a smaller decline compared with earlier weeks over the past month. Deaths also fell, declining by 8%.\r\n\r\nMore than 10 million cases were reported to the WHO last week, with South Korea, Germany, Viet Nam, Russia, and Japan reporting the most. There were more than 52 000 new deaths, and the United States continues to report the most COVID-19 fatalities of any country.\r\n\r\nIn the WHO\'s Western Pacific region, rising cases were driven by surges in South Korea, Hong Kong, Viet Nam, and New Zealand. South Korea today [9 Mar 2022] reported a new record high, with 342 466 new cases, as did Hong Kong, with 58 757 new cases. Elsewhere, China\'s cases reached a new 2-year high, with 555 new cases, and health officials in Shanghai are battling an uptick in asymptomatic cases by doing mass testing, delaying some large gatherings and shutting some public spaces, according to Reuters (<https://news.yahoo.com/shanghai-steps-defences-against-wave-070017082.html>).\r\n\r\nOf sequenced samples over the past month, 99.7% were the omicron variant, and, of those, 34.2% were the more transmissible BA.2 omicron subvariant. The WHO said its technical advisory group is aware of reports of recombinants of delta and omicron and of BA.1 and BA.2, which it said isn\'t surprising.\r\n\r\nSo far, however, sequencing hasn\'t identified any signs of rapid transmission or changes in illness severity. And only a few recombinant clusters have been reported, with little sign of spread.\r\n\r\nAt a briefing today [9 Mar 2022], WHO Director-General Tedros Adhanom Ghebreyesus, PhD, said though cases and deaths are declining and countries are loosening restrictions, the pandemic is far from over. "The virus continues to evolve, and we continue to face major obstacles in distributing vaccines, tests, and treatments everywhere they are needed," he said (<https://bit.ly/3i2uvUw>).\r\n\r\nTedros also said the WHO is concerned that several countries have drastically reduced testing, which he says clouds the ability to see where the virus is, how it\'s spreading, and how it\'s evolving.\r\n\r\nIn a related development today [9 Mar 2022], the WHO posted interim guidance on the use of rapid tests, which it says should be offered as part of overall COVID-19 testing services. The guidance addresses implementation considerations, including prioritizing populations, test accessibility, and reporting (<https://www.who.int/publications/i/item/WHO-2019-nCoV-Ag-RDTs-Self_testing-2022.1>).\r\n\r\n[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMary Marshall\r\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\r\n\r\n----\r\n[B] Hawaii: mask mandate\r\nDate: Wed 9 Mar 2022\r\nSource: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]\r\n<https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/global-drop-covid-19-continues-cases-still-high>\r\n\r\n\r\nYesterday [8 Mar 2022] Hawaii became the final US state to announce that indoor mask requirements related to the COVID-19 pandemic will end; the step takes effect on 26 Mar 2022. Puerto Rico announced earlier this week that all mask mandates on the island would be ending this week [10 Mar 2022].\r\n\r\nNew cases of COVID-19 continue to drop across the country. The United States reported 29 805 new COVID-19 cases yesterday [8 Mar 2022] and 1532 deaths, according to the Johns Hopkins COVID-19 tracker (<https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/data/cumulative-cases>). The 7-day average of new daily cases is 38 239, with 1398 daily deaths, according to the Washington Post tracker (<https://wapo.st/3w3Z0l5>). In total, the country has seen 79 385 516 COVID-19 cases in the past 2 years, including 963 079 deaths.\r\n\r\nWidespread infection with the omicron variant and vaccination has helped raised immunity in the United States. The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention COVID Data Tracker shows 65.1% of Americans are fully vaccinated against COVID-19, 76.6% have received at least one dose of vaccine, and 44.1% of fully vaccinated Americans have received a booster dose (<https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations_vacc-total-admin-rate-total>).\r\n\r\nAs the country moves on to the next phase of the pandemic, both the White House and public health experts are touting a test-to-treat program that pairs positive COVID-19 tests with antiviral drugs. Pfizer today [9 Mar 2022] launched a phase 2/3 study of its approved antiviral, Paxlovid, in kids ages 6-17.\r\n\r\n"There is a significant unmet need for outpatient treatments that can be taken by children and adolescents to help prevent progression to severe illness, including hospitalization or death," said Mikael Dolsten, chief scientific officer and president of worldwide research, development and medical at Pfizer in a press release (<https://www.pfizer.com/news/press-release/press-release-detail/pfizer-initiates-phase-23-study-novel-covid-19-oral>).\r\n\r\n"Paxlovid is already authorized or approved in many countries around the world, with more than 1.5 million treatment courses delivered thus far and 30 million expected by July [2022] to help combat this devastating disease."\r\n\r\n[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMary Marshall\r\n\r\n******\r\n[2] USA: deaths\r\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022 16:03 EST\r\nSource: The Atlantic [abridged, edited]\r\n<https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2022/03/covid-us-death-rate/626972/>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe United States reported more deaths from COVID-19 last Friday [4 Mar 2022] than deaths from Hurricane Katrina, more on any 2 recent weekdays than deaths during the 9/11 terrorist attacks, more last month [February 2022] than deaths from flu in a bad season, and more in 2 years than deaths from HIV during the 4 decades of the AIDS epidemic. At least 953 000 Americans have died from COVID, and the true toll is likely even higher because many deaths went uncounted. COVID is now the 3rd leading cause of death in the United States, after only heart disease and cancer, which are both catchall terms for many distinct diseases. The sheer scale of the tragedy strains the moral imagination. On 24 May 2020, as the United States passed 100 000 recorded deaths, The New York Times filled its front page with the names of the dead, describing their loss as "incalculable." Now the nation hurtles toward a milestone of one million. What is 10 times incalculable?\r\n\r\nMany countries have been pummeled by the coronavirus, but few have fared as poorly as the United States. Its death rate surpassed that of any other large, wealthy nation -- especially during the recent omicron surge. The Biden administration placed all its bets on a vaccine-focused strategy, rather than the multilayered protections that many experts called for, even as America lagged behind other wealthy countries in vaccinating (and boosting) its citizens -- especially elderly people, who are most vulnerable to the virus. In a study of 29 high-income countries, the United States experienced the largest decline in life expectancy in 2020 and, unlike much of Europe, did not bounce back in 2021. It was also the only country whose lowered life span was driven mainly by deaths among people under 60. Dying from COVID robbed each American of about a decade of life on average. As a whole, US life expectancy fell by 2 years -- the largest such decline in almost a century. Neither World War II nor any of the flu pandemics that followed it dented American longevity so badly.\r\n\r\nEvery American who died of COVID left an average of 9 close relatives bereaved. Roughly 9 million people -- 3% of the population -- now have a permanent hole in their world that was once filled by a parent, child, sibling, spouse, or grandparent. An estimated 149 000 children have lost a parent or caregiver. Many people were denied the familiar rituals of mourning -- bedside goodbyes, in-person funerals. Others are grieving raw and recent losses, their grief trampled amid the stampede toward normal.\r\n\r\nAfter many of the biggest disasters in American memory, including 9/11 and Hurricane Katrina, "it felt like the world stopped," Lori Peek, a sociologist at the University of Colorado at Boulder who studies disasters, told me. "On some level, we owned our failures, and there were real changes." Crossing one million deaths could offer a similar opportunity to take stock, but "900 000 deaths felt like a big threshold to me, and we didn\'t pause," Peek said. Why is that? Why were so many publications and politicians focused on reopenings in January and February [2022] -- the 4th- and 5th-deadliest months of the pandemic? Why did the CDC issue new guidelines that allowed most Americans to dispense with indoor masking when at least 1000 people had been dying of COVID every day for almost 6 straight months? If the United States faced half a year of daily hurricanes that each took 1000 lives, it is hard to imagine that the nation would decide to, quite literally, throw caution to the wind. Why, then, is COVID different?\r\n\r\nMany aspects of the pandemic work against a social reckoning. The threat -- a virus -- is invisible, and the damage it inflicts is hidden from public view. With no lapping floodwaters or smoking buildings, the tragedy becomes contestable to a degree that a natural disaster or terrorist attack cannot be. Meanwhile, many of those who witnessed COVID\'s ruin are in no position to discuss it. Healthcare workers are still reeling from "death on a scale I had never seen before," as an intensive-care nurse told me last year [2021]. The bereaved face guilt on top of sadness: "I think about the way it would run through families and tight-knit groups and the huge psychological toll as people think, Am I the one who brought it in?" Whitney Robinson, a social epidemiologist at the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, told me. And though 3% of Americans have lost a close family member to COVID, that means 97% have not. The 2 years that were shaved off of the average life span undid 2 decades of progress in health, but in 2000, "it didn\'t feel like we were living under a horrible mortality regime," Andrew Noymer, a demographer at UC Irvine, told me. "It felt normal."\r\n\r\nNo one knows how many people will die from COVID in the coming years. The number will depend on our collective behavior, how many more people can be vaccinated or boosted, the length and strength of immunity, what new variants arise, and more. Andrew Noymer, the demographer, thinks that COVID will kill fewer people per year than it has in the past 2, but will probably still be more lethal than the flu, which sets a plausible and very wide range of somewhere between 50 000 and 500 000 annual deaths. (COVID will also continue to cause long-term disability.)\r\n\r\nHow much of this extra mortality will the United States accept? The CDC\'s new guidelines provide a clue. They recommend that protective measures such as indoor masking kick in once communities pass certain thresholds of cases and hospitalizations. But the health-policy experts Joshua Salomon and Alyssa Bilinski calculated that by the time communities hit the CDC\'s thresholds, they\'d be on the path to at least 3 daily deaths per million, which equates to 1000 deaths per day nationally. And crucially, the warning lights would go off too late to prevent those deaths. "As a level of mortality the White House and CDC are willing to accept before calling for more public health protection, this is heartbreaking," Salomon said on Twitter.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Ed Yong]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nClaudinne Miller\r\nTulane Outbreak News\r\n<cmiller15@tulane.edu>\r\n\r\n[An interesting perspective on the public\'s reaction to COVID case counts and deaths worth reading in full. - Mod.LK]\r\n\r\n******\r\n[3] CIDRAP News\r\n[A] UK: BA.2\r\nDate: Thu 10 Mar 2022\r\nSource: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]\r\n<https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/covid-19-remains-high-uk-ba2-gains-ground>\r\n\r\n\r\nAn ongoing swab testing study that\'s been underway for the last 2 years to monitor COVID-19 spread in the United Kingdom revealed that, although cases are declining, they remain at a high level, with signs of a potential increase in older age-groups. The UK REACT study, done by a research team based at Imperial College London, has been tracking disease levels with swab tests.\r\n\r\nPublic health officials have urged countries to continue population monitoring for COVID-19 to assess who is getting infected and where the virus is spreading. Also, health officials closely watch patterns in Britain and other European countries because their COVID-19 trends have been a harbinger of how outbreaks could unfold elsewhere, including in the United States.\r\n\r\nFor the latest study, the group analyzed the results of nearly 95 000 swab tests that were conducted across the country from 8 Feb to 1 Mar 2022 (<https://spiral.imperial.ac.uk/bitstream/10044/1/95323/2/REACT_R18_and_SI.pdf>). Since the last report that covered roughly January [2022], prevalence of COVID-19 dropped from 4.41% to 2.88%. The researchers noted, however, that, at 2.88%, prevalence is still high -- at the 2nd-highest level since the study began in March 2020.\r\n\r\nTheir analysis of genetic sequences from 1195 samples showed that all but one was the omicron variant, and, as of 21 Feb 2022, they estimate that nearly half (47.2%) were the BA.2 subvariant, which is more transmissible than the parent omicron virus. In their last report, released in late January [2022], they found that only 6 sequences were BA.2 (<https://www.imperial.ac.uk/news/233381/fall-coronavirus-infections-england-have-stalled/>).\r\n\r\nInfection rates varied by age and region, and the team noted that levels were flat or possibly rising in people ages 55 and older. Also, the team saw high infection rates in London, followed by the southwest.\r\n\r\nJenny Harries, MD, chief executive of the UK\'s Health Security Agency, said in a statement that the data confirm that cases have declined since the omicron peak. "However, the increasing presence of the BA.2 sub-lineage of omicron and the recent slight increase in infections in those over 55 shows that the pandemic is not over and that we can expect to see COVID-19 circulating at high levels."\r\n\r\nPaul Elliott, MBBS, PhD, who directs the REACT program at Imperial College London, said the possibility that infections are rising in older adults indicates that a high number of infections will lead to more illnesses, even though the group is highly vaccinated. "So it\'s important that people continue to follow public health guidance to avoid fueling further spread of the virus."\r\n\r\nSurges continue in omicron hot spots: Hong Kong leaders appear to be stepping back from mass testing as part of handling its surge of cases, with more than 31 402 cases and 180 deaths reported today [10 Mar 2022]. Chief Executive Carrie Lam today said Hong Kong won\'t lift its ban on flights from 9 countries and reopen the city until its surge is under control, according to Reuters (<https://reut.rs/3t2mNjl>).\r\n\r\nChina\'s rise in COVID-19 activity continues, with 402 more local symptomatic cases reported as well as 435 more local asymptomatic infections, according to the National Health Commission. The largest portion were from Jilin province, which had 165 of the symptomatic cases and 179 of the asymptomatic cases (<http://en.nhc.gov.cn/2022-03/10/c_85882.htm>).\r\n\r\nIn Germany, cases topped 250 000 for the 1st time during the pandemic, according to Deutsche Welle, which said the coalition government has settled on new COVID measures to replace ones that expire on 19 Mar 2022. The new ones include basic steps such as masking on public transport and limiting regular testing to nursing homes and other vulnerable settings, though states can institute other measures if they experience future spikes (<https://www.dw.com/en/germany-new-daily-covid-19-infections-pass-250000-for-first-time/a-61075687>).\r\n\r\nNew Zealand, which is experiencing its worst surge, is feeling COVID-19 pressure on doctor\'s offices and hospitals, according to Radio New Zealand, which said general practice clinic workload has increased 50% and patient loads at Auckland hospitals are already above their worst-case scenarios (<https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/463054/watch-live-covid-19-briefing-it-is-still-going-to-be-messy-for-the-next-couple-of-weeks>).\r\n\r\n[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMary Marshall\r\n\r\n----\r\n[B] USA: coronavirus package\r\nDate: Thu 10 Mar 2022\r\nSource: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]\r\n<https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/covid-19-remains-high-uk-ba2-gains-ground>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe House of Representatives failed to include a USD 15 billion coronavirus pandemic package when it approved a USD 1.5 trillion spending bill yesterday [9 Mar 2022], signaling a major setback for the Biden administration. House Speaker Nancy Pelosi said a separate COVID relief bill will be introduced, The Hill reports (<https://thehill.com/homenews/house/597589-pelosi-says-separate-coronavirus-relief-bill-will-be-put-on-the-floor>).\r\n\r\nFor weeks the administration has petitioned lawmakers to increase funding for pandemic-related relief packages, but the war in Ukraine and plummeting case counts have pushed the pandemic to the political back burner. The 7-day average of new daily COVID-19 cases is 37 685, with 1369 daily deaths, according to The New York Times tracker (<https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2021/us/covid-cases.html>).\r\n\r\nIn related news, a new poll from the Kaiser Family Foundation (KFF) shows that 40% to 60% of Americans missed work during the omicron surge, and 6 of 10 Americans who earn USD 40 000 or less a year reported missing work owing to the most recent surge of the virus. Twenty percent of those polled said missing work had a significant impact on family finances.\r\n\r\nAs the nation enters the 3rd year of the pandemic, many companies continue to change pandemic policies. United Airlines, one of the 1st major companies to announce vaccine mandates last summer [2021], announced it will allow workers who haven\'t been vaccinated against COVID-19 for religious or medical reasons to return at the end of the month [March 2022], the Wall Street Journal reports (<https://on.wsj.com/3tSo6AC>).\r\n\r\n[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMary Marshall\r\n\r\n******\r\n[4] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 10 Mar 2022)\r\nDate: Thu 10 Mar 2022\r\nSource: WHO [abridged, edited]\r\n<https://covid19.who.int/table>\r\n\r\n\r\n*Daily case reports as of 10 Mar 2022 16:48 CET\r\n\r\nSurveillance\r\n------------\r\nWHO region (no. countries/territories):\r\nTotal confirmed cases (new cases in last 24 hours) / Total deaths (new deaths in last 24 hours)\r\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\nWestern Pacific Region (19): 30 049 923 (789 738) / 190 747 (1091)\r\nEuropean Region (61): 185 513 805 (800 258) / 1 897 675 (2392)\r\nSouth-East Asia Region (10): 56 335 465 (48 894) / 767 622 (456)\r\nEastern Mediterranean Region (22): 21 375 560 (12 670) / 337 612 (255)\r\nRegion of the Americas (54): 148 475 359 (147 136) / 2 654 909 (2865)\r\nAfrican Region (49): 8 478 759 (18 229) / 170 507 (104)\r\nCases on an international conveyance: 764 (0) / 13 (0)\r\n\r\nConfirmed cases (new cases in last 24 hours) / Total deaths (new deaths in last 24 hours)\r\nGrand total: 450 229 635 (1 816 925) / 6 019 085 (7163)\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[Data by country, area, or territory for 10 Mar 2022 can be accessed at <https://promedmail.org/wp-content/uploads/world-pdf/2022%20WHO%20Data%20Tables%20MAR10_1647026659.pdf>.\r\n\r\n- The Americas region reported 8.0% of cases and 39.9% of deaths in the past 24 hours, having reported more than 148.47 million cases, 2nd to the European region as the most severely affected region.
