20220312.8701940<div class="text1">CORONAVIRUS DISEASE 2019 UPDATE (70): CASE COUNT, UK, BA.2, USA, WHO, GLOBAL<br />****************************************************************************<br />A ProMED-mail post<br /><a href="http://www.promedmail.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.promedmail.org</a><br />ProMED-mail is a program of the<br />International Society for Infectious Diseases<br /><a href="http://www.isid.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.isid.org</a><br /><br />In this update:<br />[1] CIDRAP News<br />[A] COVID case count<br />[B] Hawaii: mask mandate<br />[2] USA: deaths<br />[3] CIDRAP News<br />[A] UK: BA.2<br />[B] USA: coronavirus package<br />[4] WHO: daily new cases reported (as of 10 Mar 2022)<br />[5] Global update: Worldometer accessed 10 Mar 2022 22:32 EST (GMT-5)<br /><br />******<br />[1] CIDRAP News<br />[A] COVID case count<br />Date: Wed 9 Mar 2022<br />Source: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]<br /><a href="https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/global-drop-covid-19-continues-cases-still-high" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/global-drop-covid-19-continues-cases-still-high</a><br /><br /><br />The world\'s COVID-19 cases declined last week for the 5th week in a row, but hotspots remain in a handful of countries, especially in Asia, the World Health Organization (WHO) said in its latest weekly update.<br /><br />Cases declined 5% last week compared to the week before, marking a smaller decline compared with earlier weeks over the past month. Deaths also fell, declining by 8%.<br /><br />More than 10 million cases were reported to the WHO last week, with South Korea, Germany, Viet Nam, Russia, and Japan reporting the most. There were more than 52 000 new deaths, and the United States continues to report the most COVID-19 fatalities of any country.<br /><br />In the WHO\'s Western Pacific region, rising cases were driven by surges in South Korea, Hong Kong, Viet Nam, and New Zealand. South Korea today [9 Mar 2022] reported a new record high, with 342 466 new cases, as did Hong Kong, with 58 757 new cases. Elsewhere, China\'s cases reached a new 2-year high, with 555 new cases, and health officials in Shanghai are battling an uptick in asymptomatic cases by doing mass testing, delaying some large gatherings and shutting some public spaces, according to Reuters (<a href="https://news.yahoo.com/shanghai-steps-defences-against-wave-070017082.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://news.yahoo.com/shanghai-steps-defences-against-wave-070017082.html</a>).<br /><br />Of sequenced samples over the past month, 99.7% were the omicron variant, and, of those, 34.2% were the more transmissible BA.2 omicron subvariant. The WHO said its technical advisory group is aware of reports of recombinants of delta and omicron and of BA.1 and BA.2, which it said isn\'t surprising.<br /><br />So far, however, sequencing hasn\'t identified any signs of rapid transmission or changes in illness severity. And only a few recombinant clusters have been reported, with little sign of spread.<br /><br />At a briefing today [9 Mar 2022], WHO Director-General Tedros Adhanom Ghebreyesus, PhD, said though cases and deaths are declining and countries are loosening restrictions, the pandemic is far from over. "The virus continues to evolve, and we continue to face major obstacles in distributing vaccines, tests, and treatments everywhere they are needed," he said (<a href="https://bit.ly/3i2uvUw" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://bit.ly/3i2uvUw</a>).<br /><br />Tedros also said the WHO is concerned that several countries have drastically reduced testing, which he says clouds the ability to see where the virus is, how it\'s spreading, and how it\'s evolving.<br /><br />In a related development today [9 Mar 2022], the WHO posted interim guidance on the use of rapid tests, which it says should be offered as part of overall COVID-19 testing services. The guidance addresses implementation considerations, including prioritizing populations, test accessibility, and reporting (<a href="https://www.who.int/publications/i/item/WHO-2019-nCoV-Ag-RDTs-Self_testing-2022.1" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.who.int/publications/i/item/WHO-2019-nCoV-Ag-RDTs-Self_testing-2022.1</a>).<br /><br />[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mary Marshall<br />&lt;mjm2020@googlemail.com><br /><br />----<br />[B] Hawaii: mask mandate<br />Date: Wed 9 Mar 2022<br />Source: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]<br /><a href="https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/global-drop-covid-19-continues-cases-still-high" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/global-drop-covid-19-continues-cases-still-high</a><br /><br /><br />Yesterday [8 Mar 2022] Hawaii became the final US state to announce that indoor mask requirements related to the COVID-19 pandemic will end; the step takes effect on 26 Mar 2022. Puerto Rico announced earlier this week that all mask mandates on the island would be ending this week [10 Mar 2022].<br /><br />New cases of COVID-19 continue to drop across the country. The United States reported 29 805 new COVID-19 cases yesterday [8 Mar 2022] and 1532 deaths, according to the Johns Hopkins COVID-19 tracker (<a href="https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/data/cumulative-cases" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/data/cumulative-cases</a>). The 7-day average of new daily cases is 38 239, with 1398 daily deaths, according to the Washington Post tracker (<a href="https://wapo.st/3w3Z0l5" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://wapo.st/3w3Z0l5</a>). In total, the country has seen 79 385 516 COVID-19 cases in the past 2 years, including 963 079 deaths.<br /><br />Widespread infection with the omicron variant and vaccination has helped raised immunity in the United States. The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention COVID Data Tracker shows 65.1% of Americans are fully vaccinated against COVID-19, 76.6% have received at least one dose of vaccine, and 44.1% of fully vaccinated Americans have received a booster dose (<a href="https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations_vacc-total-admin-rate-total" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations_vacc-total-admin-rate-total</a>).<br /><br />As the country moves on to the next phase of the pandemic, both the White House and public health experts are touting a test-to-treat program that pairs positive COVID-19 tests with antiviral drugs. Pfizer today [9 Mar 2022] launched a phase 2/3 study of its approved antiviral, Paxlovid, in kids ages 6-17.<br /><br />"There is a significant unmet need for outpatient treatments that can be taken by children and adolescents to help prevent progression to severe illness, including hospitalization or death," said Mikael Dolsten, chief scientific officer and president of worldwide research, development and medical at Pfizer in a press release (<a href="https://www.pfizer.com/news/press-release/press-release-detail/pfizer-initiates-phase-23-study-novel-covid-19-oral" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.pfizer.com/news/press-release/press-release-detail/pfizer-initiates-phase-23-study-novel-covid-19-oral</a>).<br /><br />"Paxlovid is already authorized or approved in many countries around the world, with more than 1.5 million treatment courses delivered thus far and 30 million expected by July [2022] to help combat this devastating disease."<br /><br />[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mary Marshall<br /><br />******<br />[2] USA: deaths<br />Date: Tue 8 Mar 2022 16:03 EST<br />Source: The Atlantic [abridged, edited]<br /><a href="https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2022/03/covid-us-death-rate/626972/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2022/03/covid-us-death-rate/626972/</a><br /><br /><br />The United States reported more deaths from COVID-19 last Friday [4 Mar 2022] than deaths from Hurricane Katrina, more on any 2 recent weekdays than deaths during the 9/11 terrorist attacks, more last month [February 2022] than deaths from flu in a bad season, and more in 2 years than deaths from HIV during the 4 decades of the AIDS epidemic. At least 953 000 Americans have died from COVID, and the true toll is likely even higher because many deaths went uncounted. COVID is now the 3rd leading cause of death in the United States, after only heart disease and cancer, which are both catchall terms for many distinct diseases. The sheer scale of the tragedy strains the moral imagination. On 24 May 2020, as the United States passed 100 000 recorded deaths, The New York Times filled its front page with the names of the dead, describing their loss as "incalculable." Now the nation hurtles toward a milestone of one million. What is 10 times incalculable?<br /><br />Many countries have been pummeled by the coronavirus, but few have fared as poorly as the United States. Its death rate surpassed that of any other large, wealthy nation -- especially during the recent omicron surge. The Biden administration placed all its bets on a vaccine-focused strategy, rather than the multilayered protections that many experts called for, even as America lagged behind other wealthy countries in vaccinating (and boosting) its citizens -- especially elderly people, who are most vulnerable to the virus. In a study of 29 high-income countries, the United States experienced the largest decline in life expectancy in 2020 and, unlike much of Europe, did not bounce back in 2021. It was also the only country whose lowered life span was driven mainly by deaths among people under 60. Dying from COVID robbed each American of about a decade of life on average. As a whole, US life expectancy fell by 2 years -- the largest such decline in almost a century. Neither World War II nor any of the flu pandemics that followed it dented American longevity so badly.<br /><br />Every American who died of COVID left an average of 9 close relatives bereaved. Roughly 9 million people -- 3% of the population -- now have a permanent hole in their world that was once filled by a parent, child, sibling, spouse, or grandparent. An estimated 149 000 children have lost a parent or caregiver. Many people were denied the familiar rituals of mourning -- bedside goodbyes, in-person funerals. Others are grieving raw and recent losses, their grief trampled amid the stampede toward normal.<br /><br />After many of the biggest disasters in American memory, including 9/11 and Hurricane Katrina, "it felt like the world stopped," Lori Peek, a sociologist at the University of Colorado at Boulder who studies disasters, told me. "On some level, we owned our failures, and there were real changes." Crossing one million deaths could offer a similar opportunity to take stock, but "900 000 deaths felt like a big threshold to me, and we didn\'t pause," Peek said. Why is that? Why were so many publications and politicians focused on reopenings in January and February [2022] -- the 4th- and 5th-deadliest months of the pandemic? Why did the CDC issue new guidelines that allowed most Americans to dispense with indoor masking when at least 1000 people had been dying of COVID every day for almost 6 straight months? If the United States faced half a year of daily hurricanes that each took 1000 lives, it is hard to imagine that the nation would decide to, quite literally, throw caution to the wind. Why, then, is COVID different?<br /><br />Many aspects of the pandemic work against a social reckoning. The threat -- a virus -- is invisible, and the damage it inflicts is hidden from public view. With no lapping floodwaters or smoking buildings, the tragedy becomes contestable to a degree that a natural disaster or terrorist attack cannot be. Meanwhile, many of those who witnessed COVID\'s ruin are in no position to discuss it. Healthcare workers are still reeling from "death on a scale I had never seen before," as an intensive-care nurse told me last year [2021]. The bereaved face guilt on top of sadness: "I think about the way it would run through families and tight-knit groups and the huge psychological toll as people think, Am I the one who brought it in?" Whitney Robinson, a social epidemiologist at the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, told me. And though 3% of Americans have lost a close family member to COVID, that means 97% have not. The 2 years that were shaved off of the average life span undid 2 decades of progress in health, but in 2000, "it didn\'t feel like we were living under a horrible mortality regime," Andrew Noymer, a demographer at UC Irvine, told me. "It felt normal."<br /><br />No one knows how many people will die from COVID in the coming years. The number will depend on our collective behavior, how many more people can be vaccinated or boosted, the length and strength of immunity, what new variants arise, and more. Andrew Noymer, the demographer, thinks that COVID will kill fewer people per year than it has in the past 2, but will probably still be more lethal than the flu, which sets a plausible and very wide range of somewhere between 50 000 and 500 000 annual deaths. (COVID will also continue to cause long-term disability.)<br /><br />How much of this extra mortality will the United States accept? The CDC\'s new guidelines provide a clue. They recommend that protective measures such as indoor masking kick in once communities pass certain thresholds of cases and hospitalizations. But the health-policy experts Joshua Salomon and Alyssa Bilinski calculated that by the time communities hit the CDC\'s thresholds, they\'d be on the path to at least 3 daily deaths per million, which equates to 1000 deaths per day nationally. And crucially, the warning lights would go off too late to prevent those deaths. "As a level of mortality the White House and CDC are willing to accept before calling for more public health protection, this is heartbreaking," Salomon said on Twitter.<br /><br />[Byline: Ed Yong]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Claudinne Miller<br />Tulane Outbreak News<br />&lt;cmiller15@tulane.edu><br /><br />[An interesting perspective on the public\'s reaction to COVID case counts and deaths worth reading in full. - Mod.LK]<br /><br />******<br />[3] CIDRAP News<br />[A] UK: BA.2<br />Date: Thu 10 Mar 2022<br />Source: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]<br /><a href="https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/covid-19-remains-high-uk-ba2-gains-ground" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/covid-19-remains-high-uk-ba2-gains-ground</a><br /><br /><br />An ongoing swab testing study that\'s been underway for the last 2 years to monitor COVID-19 spread in the United Kingdom revealed that, although cases are declining, they remain at a high level, with signs of a potential increase in older age-groups. The UK REACT study, done by a research team based at Imperial College London, has been tracking disease levels with swab tests.<br /><br />Public health officials have urged countries to continue population monitoring for COVID-19 to assess who is getting infected and where the virus is spreading. Also, health officials closely watch patterns in Britain and other European countries because their COVID-19 trends have been a harbinger of how outbreaks could unfold elsewhere, including in the United States.<br /><br />For the latest study, the group analyzed the results of nearly 95 000 swab tests that were conducted across the country from 8 Feb to 1 Mar 2022 (<a href="https://spiral.imperial.ac.uk/bitstream/10044/1/95323/2/REACT_R18_and_SI.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://spiral.imperial.ac.uk/bitstream/10044/1/95323/2/REACT_R18_and_SI.pdf</a>). Since the last report that covered roughly January [2022], prevalence of COVID-19 dropped from 4.41% to 2.88%. The researchers noted, however, that, at 2.88%, prevalence is still high -- at the 2nd-highest level since the study began in March 2020.<br /><br />Their analysis of genetic sequences from 1195 samples showed that all but one was the omicron variant, and, as of 21 Feb 2022, they estimate that nearly half (47.2%) were the BA.2 subvariant, which is more transmissible than the parent omicron virus. In their last report, released in late January [2022], they found that only 6 sequences were BA.2 (<a href="https://www.imperial.ac.uk/news/233381/fall-coronavirus-infections-england-have-stalled/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.imperial.ac.uk/news/233381/fall-coronavirus-infections-england-have-stalled/</a>).<br /><br />Infection rates varied by age and region, and the team noted that levels were flat or possibly rising in people ages 55 and older. Also, the team saw high infection rates in London, followed by the southwest.<br /><br />Jenny Harries, MD, chief executive of the UK\'s Health Security Agency, said in a statement that the data confirm that cases have declined since the omicron peak. "However, the increasing presence of the BA.2 sub-lineage of omicron and the recent slight increase in infections in those over 55 shows that the pandemic is not over and that we can expect to see COVID-19 circulating at high levels."<br /><br />Paul Elliott, MBBS, PhD, who directs the REACT program at Imperial College London, said the possibility that infections are rising in older adults indicates that a high number of infections will lead to more illnesses, even though the group is highly vaccinated. "So it\'s important that people continue to follow public health guidance to avoid fueling further spread of the virus."<br /><br />Surges continue in omicron hot spots: Hong Kong leaders appear to be stepping back from mass testing as part of handling its surge of cases, with more than 31 402 cases and 180 deaths reported today [10 Mar 2022]. Chief Executive Carrie Lam today said Hong Kong won\'t lift its ban on flights from 9 countries and reopen the city until its surge is under control, according to Reuters (<a href="https://reut.rs/3t2mNjl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://reut.rs/3t2mNjl</a>).<br /><br />China\'s rise in COVID-19 activity continues, with 402 more local symptomatic cases reported as well as 435 more local asymptomatic infections, according to the National Health Commission. The largest portion were from Jilin province, which had 165 of the symptomatic cases and 179 of the asymptomatic cases (<a href="http://en.nhc.gov.cn/2022-03/10/c_85882.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://en.nhc.gov.cn/2022-03/10/c_85882.htm</a>).<br /><br />In Germany, cases topped 250 000 for the 1st time during the pandemic, according to Deutsche Welle, which said the coalition government has settled on new COVID measures to replace ones that expire on 19 Mar 2022. The new ones include basic steps such as masking on public transport and limiting regular testing to nursing homes and other vulnerable settings, though states can institute other measures if they experience future spikes (<a href="https://www.dw.com/en/germany-new-daily-covid-19-infections-pass-250000-for-first-time/a-61075687" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.dw.com/en/germany-new-daily-covid-19-infections-pass-250000-for-first-time/a-61075687</a>).<br /><br />New Zealand, which is experiencing its worst surge, is feeling COVID-19 pressure on doctor\'s offices and hospitals, according to Radio New Zealand, which said general practice clinic workload has increased 50% and patient loads at Auckland hospitals are already above their worst-case scenarios (<a href="https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/463054/watch-live-covid-19-briefing-it-is-still-going-to-be-messy-for-the-next-couple-of-weeks" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/463054/watch-live-covid-19-briefing-it-is-still-going-to-be-messy-for-the-next-couple-of-weeks</a>).<br /><br />[Byline: Lisa Schnirring]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mary Marshall<br /><br />----<br />[B] USA: coronavirus package<br />Date: Thu 10 Mar 2022<br />Source: CIDRAP (Center for Infectious Disease Research and Policy) [abridged, edited]<br /><a href="https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/covid-19-remains-high-uk-ba2-gains-ground" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2022/03/covid-19-remains-high-uk-ba2-gains-ground</a><br /><br /><br />The House of Representatives failed to include a USD 15 billion coronavirus pandemic package when it approved a USD 1.5 trillion spending bill yesterday [9 Mar 2022], signaling a major setback for the Biden administration. ', 'alert_tag_id': None, 'dup_count': '0', 'dup_of': None, 'unique_string': '20220312.8701894', 'info_hash': None, 'submitted_by': '14321', 'reviewed': None, 'search_string_id': None, 'content': 'AVIAN INFLUENZA, HUMAN (10): ASIA (CHINA) H5N6, 2021\n****************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022 18:40 HKT\r\nSource: Government of the Hong Kong Special Administrative Region [edited]\r\n<https://www.info.gov.hk/gia/general/202203/08/P2022030800487.htm>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe Centre for Health Protection (CHP) of the Department of Health is today [8 Mar 2022] closely monitoring 2 human cases of avian influenza A(H5N6) in the Mainland, and again urged the public to maintain strict personal, food and environmental hygiene both locally and during travel.\r\n\r\nThe 1st case involves a 12-year-old female living in Liuzhou in Guangxi who had visited a live poultry market before onset. She developed symptoms on 17 Nov 2021 and was admitted for treatment on 20 Nov 2021. She passed away on 4 Dec 2021.\r\n\r\nThe 2nd case involves a 79-year-old man living in Liuzhou in Guangxi who had visited a live poultry market before onset. He developed symptoms on 18 Nov 2021 and was admitted for treatment on 22 Nov 2021. He passed away on 3 Dec 2021.\r\n\r\nFrom 2014 to date [8 Mar 2022], 73 human cases of avian influenza A(H5N6) have been reported by Mainland health authorities. "All novel influenza A infections, including H5N6, are notifiable infectious diseases in Hong Kong," a spokesman for the CHP said.\r\n\r\nTravellers to the Mainland or other affected areas must avoid visiting wet markets, live poultry markets or farms. They should be alert to the presence of backyard poultry when visiting relatives and friends. They should also avoid purchasing live or freshly slaughtered poultry, and avoid touching poultry/birds or their droppings. They should strictly observe personal and hand hygiene when visiting any place with live poultry.\r\n\r\nTravellers returning from affected areas should consult a doctor promptly if symptoms develop, and inform the doctor of their travel history for prompt diagnosis and treatment of potential diseases. It is essential to tell the doctor if they have seen any live poultry during travel, which may imply possible exposure to contaminated environments. This will enable the doctor to assess the possibility of avian influenza and arrange necessary investigations and appropriate treatment in a timely manner.\r\n\r\nWhile local surveillance, prevention and control measures are in place, the CHP will remain vigilant and work closely with the World Health Organization and relevant health authorities to monitor the latest developments. The public should maintain strict personal, hand, food and environmental hygiene and take heed of the advice below when handling poultry:\r\n\r\n- Avoid touching poultry, birds, animals or their droppings;\r\n- When buying live chickens, do not touch them and their droppings. Do not blow at their bottoms. Wash eggs with detergent if soiled with faecal matter and cook and consume the eggs immediately. Always wash hands thoroughly with soap and water after handling chickens and eggs;\r\n- Eggs should be cooked well until the white and yolk become firm. Do not eat raw eggs or dip cooked food into any sauce with raw eggs. Poultry should be cooked thoroughly. If there is pinkish juice running from the cooked poultry or the middle part of its bone is still red, the poultry should be cooked again until fully done;\r\n- Wash hands frequently, especially before touching the mouth, nose or eyes, before handling food or eating, and after going to the toilet, touching public installations or equipment such as escalator handrails, elevator control panels or door knobs, or when hands are dirtied by respiratory secretions after coughing or sneezing; and\r\n- Wear a mask if fever or respiratory symptoms develop, when going to a hospital or clinic, or while taking care of patients with fever or respiratory symptoms.\r\n\r\nThe public may visit the CHP\'s pages for more information: the avian influenza page, the weekly Avian Influenza Report, global statistics and affected areas of avian influenza, the Facebook Page and the YouTube Channel [see source URL above for these web links].\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMahmoud Orabi\r\n<ahstandards@gmail.com>\n\n[ProMED thanks Mahmoud Orabi for sharing this update on human cases of avian influenza A/H5N6 in China.\r\n\r\nThe above report mentions 2 new cases of avian influenza A/H5N6 in mainland China, both fatal, increasing the total cases in 2022 to 11 (although these 2 cases can technically be included in the 2021 tally). Accordingly, from 2014 to date, 73 human cases of avian influenza A(H5N6) have been reported by Mainland health authorities.\r\n\r\nAvian influenza is caused by those influenza viruses that mainly affect birds and poultry such as chickens or ducks. People mainly become infected with avian influenza virus through contact with infected birds and poultry (live or dead) or their droppings, or contact with contaminated environments (such as wet markets and live poultry markets). People in close contact with poultry are more susceptible to contracting avian influenza. The elderly, children and people with chronic illness have a higher risk of developing complications such as bronchitis and chest infections.\r\n\r\nWhenever avian influenza viruses are circulating in poultry, there is a risk for sporadic infection and small clusters of human cases due to exposure to infected poultry or contaminated environments. Therefore, sporadic human cases are not unexpected. Intensive surveillance should be continued to detect cases and early changes in transmissibility and infectivity of these viruses, as the frequency of cases appears to be increasing. - Mod.UBA\n\nProMED map:\nChina: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701894,155>]\n\n[See Also:\nAvian influenza, human (09): Asia (China) H9N2 20220306.8701796\r\nAvian influenza, human (08): href="http://www.promedmail.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.promedmail.org</a><br />ProMED-mail is a program of the<br />International Society for Infectious Diseases<br /><a href="http://www.isid.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.isid.org</a><br /><br />Date: Tue 8 Mar 2022 18:40 HKT<br />Source: Government of the Hong Kong Special Administrative Region [edited]<br /><a href="https://www.info.gov.hk/gia/general/202203/08/P2022030800487.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.info.gov.hk/gia/general/202203/08/P2022030800487.htm</a><br /><br /><br />The Centre for Health Protection (CHP) of the Department of Health is today [8 Mar 2022] closely monitoring 2 human cases of avian influenza A(H5N6) in the Mainland, and again urged the public to maintain strict personal, food and environmental hygiene both locally and during travel.<br /><br />The 1st case involves a 12-year-old female living in Liuzhou in Guangxi who had visited a live poultry market before onset. She developed symptoms on 17 Nov 2021 and was admitted for treatment on 20 Nov 2021. She passed away on 4 Dec 2021.<br /><br />The 2nd case involves a 79-year-old man living in Liuzhou in Guangxi who had visited a live poultry market before onset. He developed symptoms on 18 Nov 2021 and was admitted for treatment on 22 Nov 2021. He passed away on 3 Dec 2021.<br /><br />From 2014 to date [8 Mar 2022], 73 human cases of avian influenza A(H5N6) have been reported by Mainland health authorities. "All novel influenza A infections, including H5N6, are notifiable infectious diseases in Hong Kong," a spokesman for the CHP said.<br /><br />Travellers to the Mainland or other affected areas must avoid visiting wet markets, live poultry markets or farms. They should be alert to the presence of backyard poultry when visiting relatives and friends. They should also avoid purchasing live or freshly slaughtered poultry, and avoid touching poultry/birds or their droppings. They should strictly observe personal and hand hygiene when visiting any place with live poultry.<br /><br />Travellers returning from affected areas should consult a doctor promptly if symptoms develop, and inform the doctor of their travel history for prompt diagnosis and treatment of potential diseases. It is essential to tell the doctor if they have seen any live poultry during travel, which may imply possible exposure to contaminated environments. This will enable the doctor to assess the possibility of avian influenza and arrange necessary investigations and appropriate treatment in a timely manner.<br /><br />While local surveillance, prevention and control measures are in place, the CHP will remain vigilant and work closely with the World Health Organization and relevant health authorities to monitor the latest developments. The public should maintain strict personal, hand, food and environmental hygiene and take heed of the advice below when handling poultry:<br /><br />- Avoid touching poultry, birds, animals or their droppings;<br />- When buying live chickens, do not touch them and their droppings. Do not blow at their bottoms. Wash eggs with detergent if soiled with faecal matter and cook and consume the eggs immediately. Always wash hands thoroughly with soap and water after handling chickens and eggs;<br />- Eggs should be cooked well until the white and yolk become firm. Do not eat raw eggs or dip cooked food into any sauce with raw eggs. Poultry should be cooked thoroughly. If there is pinkish juice running from the cooked poultry or the middle part of its bone is still red, the poultry should be cooked again until fully done;<br />- Wash hands frequently, especially before touching the mouth, nose or eyes, before handling food or eating, and after going to the toilet, touching public installations or equipment such as escalator handrails, elevator control panels or door knobs, or when hands are dirtied by respiratory secretions after coughing or sneezing; and<br />- Wear a mask if fever or respiratory symptoms develop, when going to a hospital or clinic, or while taking care of patients with fever or respiratory symptoms.<br /><br />The public may visit the CHP\'s pages for more information: the avian influenza page, the weekly Avian Influenza Report, global statistics and affected areas of avian influenza, the Facebook Page and the YouTube Channel [see source URL above for these web links].<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mahmoud Orabi<br />&lt;ahstandards@gmail.com><br /><br />[ProMED thanks Mahmoud Orabi for sharing this update on human cases of avian influenza A/H5N6 in China.<br /><br />The above report mentions 2 new cases of avian influenza A/H5N6 in mainland China, both fatal, increasing the total cases in 2022 to 11 (although these 2 cases can technically be included in the 2021 tally). Accordingly, from 2014 to date, 73 human cases of avian influenza A(H5N6) have been reported by Mainland health authorities.<br /><br />Avian influenza is caused by those influenza viruses that mainly affect birds and poultry such as chickens or ducks. People mainly become infected with avian influenza virus through contact with infected birds and poultry (live or dead) or their droppings, or contact with contaminated environments (such as wet markets and live poultry markets). People in close contact with poultry are more susceptible to contracting avian influenza. The elderly, children and people with chronic illness have a higher risk of developing complications such as bronchitis and chest infections.<br /><br />Whenever avian influenza viruses are circulating in poultry, there is a risk for sporadic infection and small clusters of human cases due to exposure to infected poultry or contaminated environments. Therefore, sporadic human cases are not unexpected. Intensive surveillance should be continued to detect cases and early changes in transmissibility and infectivity of these viruses, as the frequency of cases appears to be increasing. - Mod.UBA<br Some students who ate the cake became ill. Upon the notification of the school management and teachers, 16 students were taken to hospitals in the district by ambulances. It was stated that the health status of the students who were treated with the suspicion of food poisoning was good.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMahmoud Orabi\r\n<ahstandards@gmail.com>\n\n[Knowing the incubation period between ingestion of the cake, which is thought to be the vehicle for transmission of the illnesses here, and the onset of illness can be useful in establishing a diagnosis, as is whether fever was present and what gastrointestinal symptoms (vomiting and/or diarrhea) were prominent. Turkey (03): (ZO) <br /><span class="blue">Archive Number:</span> 20220311.8701934<div class="text1">FOODBORNE ILLNESS - TURKEY (03): (ZONGULDAK)<br />********************************************<br />A ProMED-mail post<br /><a href="http://www.promedmail.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.promedmail.org</a><br />ProMED-mail is a program of the<br />International Society for Infectious Diseases<br /><a href="http://www.isid.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.isid.org</a><br /><br />Date: Thu 10 Mar 2022 17:13 TRT<br />Source: Demirören News Agency [in Turkish, machine trans., edited]<br /><a href="https://www.haberler.com/yedikleri-pastadan-rahatsizlanan-16-ogrenci-14787473-haberi/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.haberler.com/yedikleri-pastadan-rahatsizlanan-16-ogrenci-14787473-haberi/</a><br /><br /><br />A total of 16 students who ate the cake cut for their friends who were transferred to another secondary school in the Ereğli district of Zonguldak, were treated at the hospital on suspicion of food poisoning.<br /><br />In Kepez İzmirlioğulları Secondary School in Ereğli district, a cake was cut for the student who was allegedly transferred to another school. Some students who ate the cake became ill. Upon the notification of the school management and teachers, 16 students were taken to hospitals in the district by ambulances. It was stated that the health status of the students who were treated with the suspicion of food poisoning was good.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mahmoud Orabi<br />&lt;ahstandards@gmail.com><br /><br />[Knowing the incubation period between ingestion of the cake, which is thought to be the vehicle for transmission of the illnesses here, and the onset of illness can be useful in establishing a diagnosis, as is whether fever was present and what gastrointestinal symptoms (vomiting and/or diarrhea) were prominent. Most infectious etiologies would be minimized by the baking of the cake but icing of the cake afterward is a risk factor. - Mod.LL<br /><br />ProMED map:<br />Zonguldak, Turkey: <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701934,4068" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701934,4068</a>] <h2>See Also</h2>\nFoodborne illness - Fish and Game Department officials said 20 wild mallards have tested positive in Rockingham County.\r\n\r\nState veterinarian Steve Crawford said the avian flu has not been detected in any domestic birds, but he said farms and bird owners should take steps to protect their flocks. "This kills a lot of domestic birds when it infects them," Crawford said. "Our recommendation to domestic bird owners are to keep your birds away, fully separated from wild waterfowl, from their feces, from their dander."\r\n\r\nThe state Department of Agriculture said it is ramping up testing. Officials said the strain of avian flu is unlikely to affect humans.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[ProMED map of New Hampshire: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,23135>\r\nNew Hampshire county map: <https://geology.com/county-map/new-hampshire-county-map.gif>]\r\n\r\n******\r\n[2] Nebraska (Lincoln): wild goose\r\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022\r\nSource: High Plains Journal [edited]\r\n<https://www.hpj.com/livestock/hpai-confirmed-in-nebraska/article_72efe5a2-9eec-11ec-bbe6-8f1b0ddb5250.html>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe Nebraska Department of Agriculture in conjunction with the United States Department of Agriculture\'s (USDA) Wildlife Services and USDA\'s Animal and Plant Health Inspection Service have confirmed the presence of highly pathogenic H5N1 avian influenza in a wild goose near Holmes Lake in Lincoln. This is the state\'s 1st confirmed case of HPAI since 2015.\r\n\r\n"While Nebraska has not seen HPAI in a backyard or commercial poultry flock within the state this year [2022], the finding of this single goose adds Nebraska to a long list of states with confirmed cases of HPAI," said State Veterinarian Dr. Roger Dudley. "Infected wild birds can carry the disease to new areas when migrating, so we encourage backyard poultry and commercial poultry flocks to continue to remain vigilant, practice good biosecurity and report sick or dying birds immediately."\r\n\r\nThe Nebraska Department of Agriculture and the Kansas Department of Agriculture\'s (KDA) Division of Animal Health encourage poultry owners to take steps to protect their commercial and backyard flocks from avian influenza by monitoring their birds for symptoms and by implementing biosecurity practices.\r\n\r\nHighly pathogenic avian influenza is a highly contagious viral disease that can infect chickens, turkeys, and other birds and can cause severe illness and/or sudden death. HPAI has been identified in backyard flocks as well as commercial operations in neighboring states; it has not been detected in Kansas.\r\n\r\n"Protecting the poultry in the state is a high priority, and we need all poultry owners to be part of the effort to prevent the spread of disease in Kansas," said Animal Health Commissioner Justin Smith. "Our best defense is to follow strict biosecurity practices and vigilantly monitor birds for any signs of illness."\r\n\r\nAccording to the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, the recent HPAI detections do not present an immediate public health concern. No human cases of these avian influenza viruses have been detected in the United States. Avian influenza does not present a food safety risk. Poultry and eggs are safe to eat when handled and cooked properly.\r\n\r\nAs part of existing avian influenza response plans, federal and state partners are working jointly on additional surveillance and testing in areas around the affected flock. The United States has the strongest avian influenza surveillance program in the world, and USDA is working with its partners to actively look for the disease in commercial poultry operations, live bird markets and in migratory wild bird populations.\r\n\r\nFor more information about HPAI, including current status of the confirmed cases in other states as well as more information about biosecurity for your flock, go to the KDA\'s avian influenza webpage at <agriculture.ks.gov/AvianInfluenza> or call 785-564-6601.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[ProMED map of Nebraska, United States: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,23160>\r\nNebraska county map: <https://geology.com/county-map/nebraska-county-map.gif>]\r\n\r\n******\r\nCanada\r\n[3] New Brunswick (Albert County): great black-backed gull\r\nDate: Wed 9 Mar 2022 16:05 AST\r\nSource: Global News [edited]\r\n<https://globalnews.ca/news/8670483/avian-flu-new-brunswick-black-backed-gull/>\r\n\r\n\r\nNew Brunswick has detected a case of the avian flu in a great black-backed gull in the Riverview area [Albert County]. In a release, the province\'s Department of Natural Resources and Energy Development said the Canadian Wildlife Service confirmed the bird had tested positive for the highly-pathogenic avian influenza, also known as H5N1.\r\n\r\nThe strain of avian flu, which is a viral infection that can spread easily among birds, has been detected in every Atlantic province.\r\n\r\nThe release said there are several different types of avian influenza. Some wild bird species, like ducks, might carry the virus and infect other birds without getting sick themselves. Meanwhile, other wild or domestic bird species can become severely ill or die after infection.\r\n\r\n"Although the chances of people getting sick from avian influenza are extremely low, people who work around birds should take extra care," the release said.\r\n\r\nThose who encounter a sick or dead bird should contact the Department of Natural Resources and Energy Development at 1-833-301-0334, the release said.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Alex Cooke]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMahmoud Orabi\r\n<ahstandards@gmail.com>\r\n\r\n[ProMED map of New Brunswick, Canada: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,17394>\r\nNew Brunswick county map: <https://www.123rf.com/photo_23993023_new-brunswick-administrative-map.html>\r\n\r\nThe Eurasian H5N1 first detected in January 2022 in the Atlantic coast of North America continues to spread. Some wild migratory waterbirds contribute to the propagation of HPAI viruses. The current propagation of H5N1 in the Americas seems to be associated with the Atlantic Americas flyway, although the finding of an infected wild goose in Nebraska shows that the virus is already moving westward.\r\n\r\nIt is important to acknowledge that only a few bird species may play a role in the propagation of HPAI viruses. Most wild bird species, as well as poultry and other domestic birds, are neither tolerant nor resistant to HPAI viruses, and thus they become ill and do not move much, which implies that they are poor spreaders and instead may act as sentinels of viral circulation. Only a few species that migrate and can tolerate these viruses, presumably some Anseriformes, are key players driving the spread of this epidemic. - Mod.PMB]\n\n[See Also:\nAvian influenza (62): Date:</span> 2022-03-12 05:25:43 AEDT <br /><span class="blue">Subject:</span> PRO/AH/EDR> Avian influenza (65): Americas (Canada, USA) wild bird, HPAI H5N1 <br /><span class="blue">Archive Number:</span> 20220311.8701931<div class="text1">AVIAN INFLUENZA (65): AMERICAS (CANADA, USA) WILD BIRD, HPAI H5N1<br />*****************************************************************<br />A ProMED-mail post<br /><a href="http://www.promedmail.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.promedmail.org</a><br />ProMED-mail is a program of the<br />International Society for Infectious Diseases<br /><a href="http://www.isid.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.isid.org</a><br /><br />In this posting:<br />USA<br />[1] New Hampshire (Rockingham County): wild mallards<br />[2] Nebraska (Lincoln): wild goose<br />Canada<br />[3] New Brunswick (Albert County): great black-backed gull<br /><br />******<br />USA<br />[1] New Hampshire (Rockingham County): wild mallards<br />Date: Mon 28 Feb 2022 19:01 EST<br />Source: WMUR [edited]<br /><a href="https://www.wmur.com/article/highly-pathogenic-avian-flu-new-hampshire/39270445#" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.wmur.com/article/highly-pathogenic-avian-flu-new-hampshire/39270445#</a><br /><br /><br />A highly pathogenic strain of avian flu has been confirmed in New Hampshire. Fish and Game Department officials said 20 wild mallards have tested positive in Rockingham County.<br /><br />State veterinarian Steve Crawford said the avian flu has not been detected in any domestic birds, but he said farms and bird owners should take steps to protect their flocks. "This kills a lot of domestic birds when it infects them," Crawford said. "Our recommendation to domestic bird owners are to keep your birds away, fully separated from wild waterfowl, from their feces, from their dander."<br /><br />The state Department of Agriculture said it is ramping up testing. Officials said the strain of avian flu is unlikely to affect humans.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED<br /><br />[ProMED map of New Hampshire: <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,23135" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,23135</a><br />New Hampshire county map: <a href="https://geology.com/county-map/new-hampshire-county-map.gif" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://geology.com/county-map/new-hampshire-county-map.gif</a>]<br /><br />******<br />[2] Nebraska (Lincoln): wild goose<br />Date: Tue 8 Mar 2022<br />Source: High Plains Journal [edited]<br /><a href="https://www.hpj.com/livestock/hpai-confirmed-in-nebraska/article_72efe5a2-9eec-11ec-bbe6-8f1b0ddb5250.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.hpj.com/livestock/hpai-confirmed-in-nebraska/article_72efe5a2-9eec-11ec-bbe6-8f1b0ddb5250.html</a><br /><br /><br />The Nebraska Department of Agriculture in conjunction with the United States Department of Agriculture\'s (USDA) Wildlife Services and USDA\'s Animal and Plant Health Inspection Service have confirmed the presence of highly pathogenic H5N1 avian influenza in a wild goose near Holmes Lake in Lincoln. This is the state\'s 1st confirmed case of HPAI since 2015.<br /><br />"While Nebraska has not seen HPAI in a backyard or commercial poultry flock within the state this year [2022], the finding of this single goose adds Nebraska to a long list of states with confirmed cases of HPAI," said State Veterinarian Dr. Roger Dudley. "Infected wild birds can carry the disease to new areas when migrating, so we encourage backyard poultry and commercial poultry flocks to continue to remain vigilant, practice good biosecurity and report sick or dying birds immediately."<br /><br />The Nebraska Department of Agriculture and the Kansas Department of Agriculture\'s (KDA) Division of Animal Health encourage poultry owners to take steps to protect their commercial and backyard flocks from avian influenza by monitoring their birds for symptoms and by implementing biosecurity practices.<br /><br />Highly pathogenic avian influenza is a highly contagious viral disease that can infect chickens, turkeys, and other birds and can cause severe illness and/or sudden death. HPAI has been identified in backyard flocks as well as commercial operations in neighboring states; it has not been detected in Kansas.<br /><br />"Protecting the poultry in the state is a high priority, and we need all poultry owners to be part of the effort to prevent the spread of disease in Kansas," said Animal Health Commissioner Justin Smith. "Our best defense is to follow strict biosecurity practices and vigilantly monitor birds for any signs of illness."<br /><br />According to the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, the recent HPAI detections do not present an immediate public health concern. No human cases of these avian influenza viruses have been detected in the United States. Avian influenza does not present a food safety risk. Poultry and eggs are safe to eat when handled and cooked properly.<br /><br />As part of existing avian influenza response plans, federal and state partners are working jointly on additional surveillance and testing in areas around the affected flock. The United States has the strongest avian influenza surveillance program in the world, and USDA is working with its partners to actively look for the disease in commercial poultry operations, live bird markets and in migratory wild bird populations.<br /><br />For more information about HPAI, including current status of the confirmed cases in other states as well as more information about biosecurity for your flock, go to the KDA\'s avian influenza webpage at &lt;agriculture.ks.gov/AvianInfluenza> or call 785-564-6601.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED<br /><br />[ProMED map of Nebraska, United States: <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,23160" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,23160</a><br />Nebraska county map: <a href="https://geology.com/county-map/nebraska-county-map.gif" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://geology.com/county-map/nebraska-county-map.gif</a>]<br /><br />******<br />Canada<br />[3] New Brunswick (Albert County): great black-backed gull<br />Date: Wed 9 Mar 2022 16:05 AST<br />Source: Global News [edited]<br /><a href="https://globalnews.ca/news/8670483/avian-flu-new-brunswick-black-backed-gull/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://globalnews.ca/news/8670483/avian-flu-new-brunswick-black-backed-gull/</a><br /><br /><br />New Brunswick has detected a case of the avian flu in a great black-backed gull in the Riverview area [Albert County]. In a release, the province\'s Department of Natural Resources and Energy Development said the Canadian Wildlife Service confirmed the bird had tested positive for the highly-pathogenic avian influenza, also known as H5N1.<br /><br />The strain of avian flu, which is a viral infection that can spread easily among birds, has been detected in every Atlantic province.<br /><br />The release said there are several different types of avian influenza. Some wild bird species, like ducks, might carry the virus and infect other birds without getting sick themselves. Meanwhile, other wild or domestic bird species can become severely ill or die after infection.<br /><br />"Although the chances of people getting sick from avian influenza are extremely low, people who work around birds should take extra care," the release said.<br /><br />Those who encounter a sick or dead bird should contact the Department of Natural Resources and Energy Development at 1-833-301-0334, the release said.<br /><br />[Byline: Alex Cooke]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mahmoud Orabi<br />&lt;ahstandards@gmail.com><br /><br />[ProMED map of New Brunswick, Canada: <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,17394" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701931,17394</a><br />New Brunswick county map: <a href="https://www.123rf.com/photo_23993023_new-brunswick-administrative-map.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.123rf.com/photo_23993023_new-brunswick-administrative-map.html</a><br /><br />The Eurasian H5N1 first detected in January 2022 in the Atlantic coast of North America continues to spread. Some wild migratory waterbirds contribute to the propagation of HPAI viruses. The current propagation of H5N1 in the Americas seems to be associated with the Atlantic Americas flyway, although the finding of an infected wild goose in Nebraska shows that the virus is already moving westward.<br /><br />It is important to acknowledge that only a few bird species may play a role in the propagation of HPAI viruses. Most wild bird species, as well as poultry and other domestic birds, are neither tolerant nor resistant to HPAI viruses, and thus they become ill and do not move much, which implies that they are poor spreaders and instead may act as sentinels of viral circulation. Only a few species that migrate and can tolerate these viruses, presumably some Anseriformes, are key players driving the spread of this epidemic. - Mod.PMB] <h2>See Also</h2>\nAvian influenza (62): There are 3 cVDPV2 cases in the country in 2021. \r\n \r\nMadagascar\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 1 (cVDPV1) was reported this week. The number of 2021 cases remains 13. There is 1 case in 2022.\r\n \r\nMalawi\r\n• No case of WPV1 was reported this week. Last month, the country reported the 1st WPV1 case in the continent since 2016.\r\n• In response to confirmation of the WPV1 outbreak in the country, the Government of Malawi declared the outbreak a national public health emergency and activated the emergency operations centre to coordinate outbreak response. Global and regional support from the GPEI Rapid Response Team are in-country to support planning, implementing and monitoring of response.\r\n• The response plan includes at least 4 large-scale outbreak response campaigns with bivalent OPV, including as part of a subregional, cross-border response together with Mozambique, Tanzania and Zambia, to reach more than 9 million children in the sub region with polio vaccine.\r\n• Training and coordination is ongoing across all levels, including at district levels, to ensure high-quality planning for the upcoming response.\r\n• Health promotion, advocacy and communication activities are focusing on producing and disseminating high-quality materials, including public service announcements and radio jingles\r\n• Vaccine distribution and management training are underway.\r\n• Surveillance continues to be strengthened, including by supplementing AFP surveillance with roll-out of environmental surveillance, with 8 sites having been established thus far.\r\n• Daily tracking of SIA preparedness across all levels is being coordinated by the emergency operations centre.\r\n \r\nMali\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. No cases have been reported in 2021.\r\n \r\nMauritania\r\n• 1 cVDPV2 positive environmental sample was reported in Nouakchott Ouest. There are 7 positive samples linked to the Jigawa outbreak in 2021.\r\n \r\nMozambique\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 2 cases reported in 2021.\r\n• In response to the confirmed cVDPV2 outbreak in the country, the Minister of Health declared the outbreak to be a national public health emergency in February [2022].\r\n• Outbreak response will be implemented, through high-quality SIAs covered the infected provinces. A national emergency operations centre has been established to coordinate outbreak response activities.\r\n• Mozambique will also participate in multi-country, subregional emergency outbreak response with Malawi and other countries, in response to the recent detection of WPV1 in Malawi.\r\n• Surveillance for AFP in high-risk and infected areas is being intensified.\r\n \r\nNiger\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. The number of 2021 cases remains 15.\r\n \r\nNigeria\r\n• 1 case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week making it the 2nd case in 2022. The number of 2021 cases remains 415.\r\n\r\nOccupied Palestinian territory\r\n• 8 cVDPV3 positive environmental samples were reported; 1 in Ramallah and 7 in the West Bank. These are the 1st ES samples to be reported in the territory.\r\n \r\n Senegal\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 17 cases reported in 2021.\r\n\r\nSierra Leone\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 5 cases reported in 2021. \r\n\r\nSomalia\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There is 1 case reported in 2022 and 1 case in 2021.\r\n \r\nSouth Sudan\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 9 cVDPV2 cases reported in 2021.\r\n \r\nSudan\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. No cases have been reported in 2021.\r\n\r\nTajikistan\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 32 cases reported in 2021.\r\n \r\nTogo\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. No cases have been reported in 2021.\r\n \r\nUganda\r\n• No cVDPV2 positive environmental sample was reported this week. There are 2 positive samples linked to the N'Djamena outbreak in Chad reported in 2021.\r\n \r\nUkraine\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 2 cases reported in 2021.\r\n• The GPEI is extremely concerned about the unfolding effects of the current crisis in Ukraine on the country's health system. A functioning health system must be kept neutral and protected from all political or security issues affecting countries, to ensure that people have continued access to critical and essential care. At the same time, we have seen time and again that large-scale population movements, insecurity and hampered access contribute greatly to the emergence and/or spread of infectious diseases, such as polio.\r\n• A national supplemental polio immunization campaign targeting nearly 140 000 children throughout Ukraine who had not been vaccinated against polio began on 1 Feb 2022, but is currently paused, as health authorities have shifted focus towards emergency services. Surveillance to detect and report new cases of polio is also disrupted, increasing the risk of undetected spread of the disease among vulnerable populations. The GPEI is working to urgently develop contingency plans to support Ukraine and prevent further spread of polio.\r\n• The GPEI has a long history of working in a variety of complex environments and will continue to adapt its operations to the reality on the ground, to the degree possible, without compromising on the safety and security of health workers. At the same time, immunization and surveillance is being assessed in neighbouring countries, to minimize the risk and consequences of any potential infectious disease emergence/spread resulting from the current large-scale population movements. It is critical that necessary resources are mobilized and made available to assist with the humanitarian needs, including relief, disease response/prevention efforts both in Ukraine and in neighbouring countries.\r\n \r\nYemen\r\n• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 13 cVDPV2 cases and 3 cVDPV1 cases reported in 2021.\r\n \r\nOfficially reported WPV1 and cVDPV cases as of [8 Mar 2022]\r\nWild poliovirus (WPV)\r\n- Total global WPV1 cases in 2022: 1 (compared with 2 for the same period in 2021)\r\n- Total global WPV1 cases in 2021: 6\r\n\r\nCirculating vaccine-derived poliovirus (cVDPV) cases\r\n- Total global cVDPV cases in 2022: 6 (compared with 30 for the same period in 2021)\r\n- Total global cVDPV cases in 2021: 637\r\n \r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[This week's report has 3 countries reporting AFP cases associated with cVDPV - cVDPV2 in DR Congo and Nigeria and cVDPV3 in Israel. Other areas with documented cVDPVs through environmental sampling include cVDPV2 in Cote d'Ivoire and Mauritania, and cVDPV3 in the Palestinian Authority.\r\n\r\nUnfortunately the charts showing the virus isolates and date of most recent isolate by source (AFP case other humans (non-AFP infected) and environmental samples) for WPVs and cVDPVs for this past week (as of 9 Mar 2022) have not been posted as yet (see <https://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/this-week/circulating-vaccine-derived-poliovirus/>). It would be interesting to see the time table of positive samples... did the ESs pre-date the identification of the AFP case (the answer seems to be yes reading between the lines) and did the positive ESs in the Palestinian Authority precede, follow or were basically chronologically the same? \r\n\r\nAccording to the Polio Eradication Initiative website, as of 1 Mar 2022 there had only been 2 countries reporting isolation of cVDPV3 since 2016 - China (positive ES 25 Jan 2021) and Somalia (positive AFP case 7 Sep 2018). Unless there has been undetected circulation in those countries for 1 and 3 years, respectively, it is highly likely this virus is a new outbreak in the region. \r\n\r\nOther information not mentioned is whether the cVDPV3 isolates in the Palestinian Authority are genetically related to those identified in Israel. \r\n\r\nA map showing Israel and the Palestinian Authority can be found at: <https://www.nationsonline.org/oneworld/map/israel_map.htm>.\r\n\r\nA map showing the locations of each confirmed case of polio worldwide in the past 12 months can be found at <https://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/>. One can see cases of cVDPV in a band across Africa and in Israel, Ukraine, Tajikistan, Afghanistan and Pakistan, cVDPV1 in Madagascar and Yemen, and WPV1 in Afghanistan and Pakistan. - Mod.MPP]\r\n\r\n******\r\n[2] Israel, Palestine cVDPV3\r\nDate: Thu 10 Mar 2022\r\nSource: Polio Eradication Initiative [edited]\r\n<https://polioeradication.org/news-post/circulating-vaccine-derived-poliovirus-confirmed-in-israel-and-occupied-palestinian-territory/>\r\n\r\n\r\nCirculating vaccine-derived poliovirus confirmed in Israel and the occupied Palestinian territory\r\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\nOn Monday [7 Mar 2022], a case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 3 (cVDPV3) was confirmed in an unvaccinated girl aged 3 years and 9 months in Israel. The girl had developed acute flaccid paralysis and upon testing of her stool, poliovirus was confirmed. Further testing of the poliovirus isolated from the girl revealed genetic links to VDPV3-strains detected in environmental samples collected from sites in in Israel and the occupied Palestinian territory between September 2021 and January 2022. These isolates, previously classified as ambiguous VDPV3, have now been reclassified as circulating VDPV3 (cVDPV3). This confirms an outbreak of cVDPV3 in both Israel and the occupied Palestinian territory.\r\n\r\nLocal health authorities are conducting field, epidemiological and virological investigations, to determine more clearly the source and origin of the isolated virus, and potential risk of further spread associated with it.\r\n\r\nExperts from the headquarters, regional and country offices of the Global Polio Eradication Initiative (GPEI) partnership, which includes WHO, Rotary International (RI), the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC), the United Nations Children's Fund (UNICEF), Bill & Melinda Gates Foundation (BMGF) and the Global Alliance for Vaccine and Immunization (GAVI), are working together to help ensure an appropriate response and cessation of this outbreak.\r\n\r\nDetection of this cVDPV3 underscores the importance of strong disease surveillance and high population immunity levels, in order to minimize the risk and consequences of any poliovirus introduction or emergence.\r\n\r\nThe GPEI partnership urges all health authorities to enhance surveillance for poliovirus and implement enhanced vaccination response to prevent further transmission, so that no child is at risk of lifelong paralysis from a disease that can so easily be prevented. GPEI is committed to assisting the health authorities in their efforts to stop the cVDPV3 outbreak.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\n\n[Our thanks to Helen Branswell for alerting us to the identification of cVDPV3 as the causative virus in this event. We await further information on the provenance of the cVDPV3 identified. There are 2 cases reported in 2021.<br />• The GPEI is extremely concerned about the unfolding effects of the current crisis in Ukraine on the country\'s health system. A functioning health system must be kept neutral and protected from all political or security issues affecting countries, to ensure that people have continued access to critical and essential care. At the same time, we have seen time and again that large-scale population movements, insecurity and hampered access contribute greatly to the emergence and/or spread of infectious diseases, such as polio.<br />• A national supplemental polio immunization campaign targeting nearly 140 000 children throughout Ukraine who had not been vaccinated against polio began on 1 Feb 2022, but is currently paused, as health authorities have shifted focus towards emergency services. Surveillance to detect and report new cases of polio is also disrupted, increasing the risk of undetected spread of the disease among vulnerable populations. The GPEI is working to urgently develop contingency plans to support Ukraine and prevent further spread of polio.<br />• The GPEI has a long history of working in a variety of complex environments and will continue to adapt its operations to the reality on the ground, to the degree possible, without compromising on the safety and security of health workers. At the same time, immunization and surveillance is being assessed in neighbouring countries, to minimize the risk and consequences of any potential infectious disease emergence/spread resulting from the current large-scale population movements. It is critical that necessary resources are mobilized and made available to assist with the humanitarian needs, including relief, disease response/prevention efforts both in Ukraine and in neighbouring countries.<br /> <br />Yemen<br />• No case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) was reported this week. There are 13 cVDPV2 cases and 3 cVDPV1 cases reported in 2021.<br /> <br />Officially reported WPV1 and cVDPV cases as of [8 Mar 2022]<br />Wild poliovirus (WPV)<br />- Total global WPV1 cases in 2022: 1 (compared with 2 for the same period in 2021)<br />- Total global WPV1 cases in 2021: 6<br /><br />Circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus (cVDPV) cases<br />- Total global cVDPV cases in 2022: 6 (compared with 30 for the same period in 2021)<br />- Total global cVDPV cases in 2021: 637<br /> <br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED<br /><br />[This week\'s report has 3 countries reporting AFP cases associated with cVDPV - cVDPV2 in DR Congo and Nigeria and cVDPV3 in Israel. Other areas with documented cVDPVs through environmental sampling include cVDPV2 in Cote d\'Ivoire and Mauritania, and cVDPV3 in the Palestinian Authority.<br /><br />Unfortunately the charts showing the virus isolates and date of most recent isolate by source (AFP case other humans (non-AFP infected) and environmental samples) for WPVs and cVDPVs for this past week (as of 9 Mar 2022) have not been posted as yet (see <a href="https://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/this-week/circulating-vaccine-derived-poliovirus/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/this-week/circulating-vaccine-derived-poliovirus/</a>). It would be interesting to see the time table of positive samples... did the ESs pre-date the identification of the AFP case (the answer seems to be yes reading between the lines) and did the positive ESs in the Palestinian Authority precede, follow or were basically chronologically the same? <br /><br />According to the Polio Eradication Initiative website, as of 1 Mar 2022 there had only been 2 countries reporting isolation of cVDPV3 since 2016 - China (positive ES 25 Jan 2021) and Somalia (positive AFP case 7 Sep 2018). Unless there has been undetected circulation in those countries for 1 and 3 years, respectively, it is highly likely this virus is a new outbreak in the region. <br /><br />Other information not mentioned is whether the cVDPV3 isolates in the Palestinian Authority are genetically related to those identified in Israel. <br /><br />A map showing Israel and the Palestinian Authority can be found at: <a href="https://www.nationsonline.org/oneworld/map/israel_map.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.nationsonline.org/oneworld/map/israel_map.htm</a>.<br /><br />A map showing the locations of each confirmed case of polio worldwide in the past 12 months can be found at <a href="https://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/</a>. One can see cases of cVDPV in a band across Africa and in Israel, Ukraine, Tajikistan, Afghanistan and Pakistan, cVDPV1 in Madagascar and Yemen, and WPV1 in Afghanistan and Pakistan. - Mod.MPP]<br /><br />******<br />[2] Israel, Palestine cVDPV3<br />Date: Thu 10 Mar 2022<br />Source: Polio Eradication Initiative [edited]<br /><a href="https://polioeradication.org/news-post/circulating-vaccine-derived-poliovirus-confirmed-in-israel-and-occupied-palestinian-territory/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://polioeradication.org/news-post/circulating-vaccine-derived-poliovirus-confirmed-in-israel-and-occupied-palestinian-territory/</a><br /><br /><br />Circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus confirmed in Israel and the occupied Palestinian territory<br />--------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br />On Monday [7 Mar 2022], a case of circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 3 (cVDPV3) was confirmed in an unvaccinated girl aged 3 years and 9 months in Israel. The girl had developed acute flaccid paralysis and upon testing of her stool, poliovirus was confirmed. Further testing of the poliovirus isolated from the girl revealed genetic links to VDPV3-strains detected in environmental samples collected from sites in in Israel and the occupied Palestinian territory between September 2021 and January 2022. These isolates, previously classified as ambiguous VDPV3, have now been reclassified as circulating VDPV3 (cVDPV3). This confirms an outbreak of cVDPV3 in both Israel and the occupied Palestinian territory.<br /><br />Local health authorities are conducting field, epidemiological and virological investigations, to determine more clearly the source and origin of the isolated virus, and potential risk of further spread associated with it.<br /><br />Experts from the headquarters, regional and country offices of the Global Polio Eradication Initiative (GPEI) partnership, which includes WHO, Rotary International (RI), the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC), the United Nations Children\'s Fund (UNICEF), Bill & Melinda Gates Foundation (BMGF) and the Global Alliance for Vaccine and Immunization (GAVI), are working together to help ensure an appropriate response and cessation of this outbreak.<br /><br />Detection of this cVDPV3 underscores the importance of strong disease surveillance and high population immunity levels, in order to minimize the risk and consequences of any poliovirus introduction or emergence.<br /><br />The GPEI partnership urges all health authorities to enhance surveillance for poliovirus and implement enhanced vaccination response to prevent further transmission, so that no child is at risk of lifelong paralysis from a disease that can so easily be prevented. GPEI is committed to assisting the health authorities in their efforts to stop the cVDPV3 outbreak.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED<br /><br />[Our thanks to Helen Branswell for alerting us to the identification of cVDPV3 as the causative virus in this event. We await further information on the provenance of the cVDPV3 identified. Mod. TY, edited]\r\n<https://diariodeavisos.elespanol.com/2022/03/detectan-el-mosquito-aedes-aegypti-en-la-palma-sin-dengue-ni-zika/>\r\n\r\n\r\nThe Canary\'s Entomological Surveillance System has detected 2 larvae of the _Aedes aegypti_ mosquito on La Palma Island, but this is "an isolated finding" and they do not have viruses that carry transmissible diseases, the Ministry of Health reported.\r\n\r\n_Aedes aegypti_, known as the yellow fever mosquito, "is a vector that transmits viral diseases in other geographic areas where these pathogens are endemic, which is not the case in the Canary Islands."\r\n\r\nThe sequencing of the larvae has verified that they do not contain viruses that carry transmissible diseases, but in any case "we must also activate the detection and surveillance protocol."\r\n\r\nIn 2017, the Entomological Surveillance System of the Canary Islands detected the presence of this mosquito in Fuerteventura Island, from where it was definitively eradicated (see Invasive mosquito - Spain: (CN) 20171214.5503487).\r\n\r\nIn this case, the presence of invasive mosquito larvae "has been detected in a specific area" of the island of La Palma, so residents will be surveyed and possible breeding sites inspected and located, as well as more traps will be placed in the area.\r\n\r\nThe Ministry of Health points out that the surveillance system allows the early detection of invasive mosquito larvae and eggs, "before their presence has been reported or before they have caused bites in the island\'s population."\r\n\r\n"All the necessary information is being compiled to limit, verify and, where appropriate, eradicate the presence of this mosquito on the island," the Ministry states.\r\n\r\nThe presence of the mosquito "does not mean that there is transmission of [of viruses that cause] diseases, such as dengue, Zika, yellow fever or chikungunya, since these [viruses] are not present in our territory, except for sporadic imported cases."\r\n\r\nThe Surveillance and Public Health System team, coordinated by the General Directorate of Public Health in collaboration with the Directorate of the La Palma Health Area is carrying out initial preventive action.\r\n\r\nThe placement of traps has been expanded at points considered to be at greatest risk, such as greenhouses, banana packing plants, cemeteries, and tire dumps, in addition to the port and airport, where they are currently located by protocol.\r\n\r\n_A. aegypti_ mosquitoes are black with [silver] stripes and smaller than the usual ones in the Canary Islands. They appear more in urban environments and have become adapted to reproduce in small water collection sites generated by people.\r\n\r\nThey usually bite during the day and not at night and their bite generates a strong inflammatory reaction that is accompanied by a great irritation. They move nimbly close to the ground and no buzzing is heard.\r\n\r\nThe female mosquitoes are the ones that bite, since they need to feed on blood to reproduce. They also need water as breeding sites to complete their development. They lay their eggs in the water, from which the larvae emerge, then transform into pupae (both are aquatic) and finally become adult mosquitoes.\r\n\r\nMosquitoes that bite humans need to be breeding very close to people. That is why the most effective measure against them is to monitor or eliminate their breeding sites.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMahmoud Orabi\r\n<ahstandards@gmail.com>\n\n[ProMED-mail thanks Mahmoud Orabi for submitting this report.\r\n\r\nThis is yet another example of movement of _Aedes aegypti_ to a new location. The possible mechanism of transport in this case is not mentioned. This is the 2nd report of the appearance of _A. aegypti_ in the Canary Islands. The 1st was in 2017. The entomological surveillance in the Islands has been very effective in detecting the presence of _A. aegypti_ very early on and eliminating them. The risk of new introductions of this mosquito is ongoing. One hopes that surveillance and response will continue to be successful in preventing the establishment of this mosquito or others in the Canary Islands. - Mod.TY]\n\n[See Also:\n2017\r\n----\r\nInvasive mosquito - Spain: (CN) 20171214.5503487]\n.................................................jh/ty/mj/jh'}, 'post': '<span class="printable"><p><img src="https://promedmail.org/wp-content/plugins/promed-latest-post/assets/images/printer.gif"/><a href="javascript:;" onclick="window.open(\'https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=8701924\');"> View printable version</a> &nbsp;
