{'postinfo': {'alert_id': '8701917', 'feed_id': '1', 'summary': 'PRO/EDR> Gonorrhea - Australia: (VI) women, urban poor, RFI', 'summary_en': None, 'summary_es': None, 'summary_fr': None, 'summary_ru': None, 'summary_zh': None, 'summary_pt': None, 'summary_ar': None, 'summary_th': None, 'summary_vi': None, 'summary_id': None, 'href': '?id=20220310.8701917', 'source_id': None, 'info_blob': None, 'info_blob2': None, 'issue_date': '2022-03-10 18:11:09', 'load_date': '2022-03-10 18:11:09', 'incident_date': None, 'descr': "An outbreak of a sexually transmitted infection is rapidly spreading through Melbourne's outer suburbs, leaving experts baffled as to the cause. New research from Alfred Health has revealed the areas of Brimbank and Melton in the city's north-west, and Casey in the city's south-east, are showing a surging number of gonorrhea cases.<br/><br/>The study is the 1st of its kind to track the geographical distribution of the STI [sexually transmitted infection] over 10 years and found lower income areas ", 'alert_tag_id': None, 'dup_count': '0', 'dup_of': None, 'unique_string': '20220310.8701917', 'info_hash': None, 'submitted_by': '3404', 'reviewed': None, 'search_string_id': None, 'content': 'GONORRHEA - AUSTRALIA: (VICTORIA) WOMEN, URBAN POOR, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n****************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\n[1]\r\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022 06:20 GMT\r\nSource: Daily mail [edited]\r\n<https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-10588693/Expert-baffled-five-fold-increase-sexually-transmitted-disease-women-Melbourne-suburbs.html>\r\n\r\n\r\nAn outbreak of a sexually transmitted infection is rapidly spreading through Melbourne\'s outer suburbs, leaving experts baffled as to the cause. New research from Alfred Health has revealed the areas of Brimbank and Melton in the city\'s north-west, and Casey in the city\'s south-east, are showing a surging number of gonorrhea cases.\r\n\r\nThe study is the 1st of its kind to track the geographical distribution of the STI [sexually transmitted infection] over 10 years and found lower income areas further from Melbourne\'s CBD [Central Business District] were more susceptible.\r\n\r\n\'Why this is occurring is the million-dollar question,\' Alfred Health epidemiologist and biostatistician Eric Chow told The Age. Historically, gonorrhoea was mostly circulated among men who had sex with other men but the research also shows women are getting infected at an alarming rate.\r\n\r\nThe infection, also known as \'the clap\' is caused by bacteria which colonises the genital region and can be treated by antibiotics. But, if left untreated, it can cause infertility in women. Worryingly, there is also an antibiotic resistant version that has been detected in cases in every Australian state and territory.\r\n\r\nVictoria recorded more than 7000 cases last year [2021] but experts say the real number is likely much higher with many cases not showing symptoms and going undetected.\r\n\r\nAssociate Professor Chow said since 2010, gonorrhoea infections in females had increased more than 5-fold. The number rose from 291 to almost 1600 last year [2021], showing heterosexual gonorrhoea was endemic in Australia.\r\n\r\nHe said lockdowns had not seemed to slow the spread of the infection, particularly in lower socioeconomic areas. \'It\'s just gone up exponentially among women in the outer suburbs of Melbourne,\' Mr Chow said. \'We really don\'t know whether it is because of the lack of sexual health literacy and services, or whether it is more risky behaviour in those areas. But definitely the outer suburbs are becoming our greatest area of concern.\'\r\n\r\nThe Alfred Institute has established 3 general practice clinics in the Melbourne suburbs of Hillside, Tarneit, and Clayton to combat the outbreak.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Brett Lackey]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\r\n\r\n******\r\n[2]\r\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022 11:55 AEDT\r\nSource: The Age [edited]\r\n<https://www.theage.com.au/national/gonorrhoea-epidemic-hits-citys-outer-suburbs-20220302-p5a0vv.html>\r\n\r\n\r\nOutbreaks of gonorrhoea are spreading rapidly through Melbourne\'s outer suburbs, with doctors warning that the municipalities of Melton, Casey, and Brimbank are now battling an evolving epidemic of the sexually transmitted disease that has alarmed and perplexed experts. New research from Alfred Health has, for the 1st time, tracked the geographical distribution of gonorrhoea over a decade, finding growing clusters of the sexually transmitted infection were infiltrating some of the most socioeconomically disadvantaged areas of Melbourne.\r\n\r\nAlfred Health epidemiologist and biostatistician Eric Chow, who led the study, said while the disease previously circulated among men who had sex with other men, a growing number of women were becoming infected. "Why this is occurring is the million-dollar question," Associate Professor Chow said. "We really don\'t know whether it is because of the lack of sexual health literacy and services, or whether it is more risky behaviour in those areas. But definitely, the outer suburbs are becoming our greatest area of concern."\r\n\r\nVictoria recorded more than 7000 gonorrhoea cases last year [2021], compared to roughly 6500 cases in 2020, but screening of people without symptoms plummeted by almost 70 per cent during the pandemic and experts warn the true number of infections is probably far higher than official state government figures.\r\n\r\nAssociate Professor Chow said the study found that since 2010, gonorrhoea infections in females had increased more than 5-fold from 291 in a year, to almost 1600 last year [2021], showing heterosexual gonorrhoea was now endemic in Australia.\r\n\r\nThe research comes as Victoria battles a wave of syphilis outbreaks that has led to at least 4 fetal deaths in Victoria in recent years after several babies contracted syphilis from their mothers. The sharp rise in deaths followed a 14-year absence of fatal cases. Exactly why this is occurring remains unclear. Growing research suggests casual sexual activity reduced and dating app use declined during the pandemic.\r\n\r\nAssociate Professor Chow did say increased sexual promiscuity linked to the explosion in dating apps might have been one factor that had led to a sustained increase in STIs. But he believes the issue is far more complex than that, noting there was a rise in gonorrhoea in the early 2010s, before the online introduction apps became commonplace. "One of the most concerning things to us is the increase in the disease among heterosexual men and women," Associate Professor Chow said. "It\'s just gone up exponentially among women in the outer suburbs of Melbourne."\r\n\r\nThe research found that there was the sharpest rise in cases between 2017 and 2019 with 24 825 notified gonorrhoea cases in Victoria, of which one in 5 were women, 13 per cent were heterosexual males, and about 42 per cent were men who had sex with men. It also found rates of infections of the STI had more than tripled in the outer suburbs of Melbourne.\r\n\r\nInfections of gonorrhoea among men who have sex with men are concentrated in inner metropolitan Melbourne, and experts said research showed this cohort were the most likely to be regularly screened for STIs, which may explain the higher rates of detection.\r\n\r\nBut of increasing concern to doctors, is the growing number of cases among women concentrated in the outer suburbs, where there remained a worrying lack of health services screening for sexually transmitted diseases and Associate Professor Chow said there was an urgent need for more support.\r\n\r\nData from the Victorian government\'s infectious diseases surveillance report shows the City of Yarra, which includes inner-city suburbs Fitzroy, Collingwood, and Abbotsford, had the highest increase in cases, reporting 535 infections last year [2021], compared to 380 in 2020.\r\n\r\nProblematically, gonorrhoea has become increasingly immune to antibiotics and a drug-resistant strain of the bacteria, dubbed a "super-superbug", has been detected in every Australian state and territory. Associate Professor Chow said there were international concerns about rising resistance to the antibiotic drugs prescribed to treat gonorrhoea. "This is quite concerning because it will make the infection more difficult to treat," he said.\r\n\r\nAssociate Professor Marcus Chen, from Melbourne Sexual Health Centre, said experts were now examining where Victorians were acquiring gonorrhoea, noting a limitation of the recent study was that it was based on the residence of the notified cases. "We\'re getting a feeling there\'s an element of marginalisation linked to outbreaks," Associate Professor Chen said. "There\'s obviously something driving new infections, but if testing and treatment were sufficient to offset it, then you wouldn\'t get a worsening epidemic, which is what we are seeing."\r\n\r\n[Byline: Melissa Cunningham]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\n\n["Melbourne is the capital and most populous city in the Australian state of Victoria and the 2nd most populous city in Australia." (<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melbourne>). A ProMED map of Australia can be accessed at <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701917,295>.\r\n\r\nIn May 2021, ProMED posted a news report of an outbreak of syphilis in urban poor women in Melbourne\'s outer suburbs (Brimbank and Melton to the city\'s northwest, and Casey, to the city\'s southeast) that was associated with an increase in cases of congenital and ocular syphilis (see ProMED post Syphilis - Australia: (VI) ocular, women, congenital, urban poor, genotyping, alert 20210518.8367315). In that outbreak, scientists were said to be using genomic sequencing for the 1st time to track syphilis cases.\r\n\r\nThe May 2021 report attributed the increase in STDs in lower-socio economic communities in Melbourne\'s outer suburbs in part to barriers in accessing healthcare. A report on the effects that social and economic conditions in these areas of Melbourne have on health care can be found in a report entitled "HealthWest Partnership response to the Senate Committees on Community Affairs: Australia\'s domestic response to the World Health Organization\'s (WHO) Commission on Social Determinants of Health report -- Closing the gap within a generation" (<https://bit.ly/3yiFwrI>).\r\n\r\nThe current news reports above are now reporting an outbreak of gonorrhea, another sexually transmitted disease (STD), in the same Melbourne outer suburbs of Brimbank, Melton, and Casey as previously reported for syphilis, among women apparently in the same demographic group that was affected by syphilis. A map showing the location of these 3 Melbourne suburbs can be found at <https://www.theage.com.au/national/gonorrhoea-epidemic-hits-citys-outer-suburbs-20220302-p5a0vv.html>. We are not told if antibiotic resistant strains of gonococci are involved in this outbreak.\r\n\r\nIn recent ProMED posts, illicit drug use, namely methamphetamine, has been cited as a contributing factor to recent increases in STDs in women in both the United States and Canada (see the "See Also" section below). Illicit drug use is associated with sexual behaviors that increase the risk of acquiring syphilis and other sexually transmitted diseases, including having multiple anonymous sex partners, inconsistent condom use, and exchange of sex for drugs or money.\r\n\r\nMore information on this outbreak of STDs in Melbourne suburbs would be appreciated from knowledgeable sources. - Australia: (VI) women, urban poor, RFI <br /><span class="blue">Archive Number:</span> 20220310.8701917<div class="text1">GONORRHEA - AUSTRALIA: (VICTORIA) WOMEN, URBAN POOR, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION<br />****************************************************************************<br />A ProMED-mail post<br /><a href="http://www.promedmail.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.promedmail.org</a><br />ProMED-mail is a program of the<br />International Society for Infectious Diseases<br /><a href="http://www.isid.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.isid.org</a><br /><br />[1]<br />Date: Tue 8 Mar 2022 06:20 GMT<br />Source: Daily mail [edited]<br /><a href="https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-10588693/Expert-baffled-five-fold-increase-sexually-transmitted-disease-women-Melbourne-suburbs.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-10588693/Expert-baffled-five-fold-increase-sexually-transmitted-disease-women-Melbourne-suburbs.html</a><br /><br /><br />An outbreak of a sexually transmitted infection is rapidly spreading through Melbourne\'s outer suburbs, leaving experts baffled as to the cause. New research from Alfred Health has revealed the areas of Brimbank and Melton in the city\'s north-west, and Casey in the city\'s south-east, are showing a surging number of gonorrhea cases.<br /><br />The study is the 1st of its kind to track the geographical distribution of the STI [sexually transmitted infection] over 10 years and found lower income areas further from Melbourne\'s CBD [Central Business District] were more susceptible.<br /><br />\'Why this is occurring is the million-dollar question,\' Alfred Health epidemiologist and biostatistician Eric Chow told The Age. Historically, gonorrhoea was mostly circulated among men who had sex with other men but the research also shows women are getting infected at an alarming rate.<br /><br />The infection, also known as \'the clap\' is caused by bacteria which colonises the genital region and can be treated by antibiotics. But, if left untreated, it can cause infertility in women. Worryingly, there is also an antibiotic resistant version that has been detected in cases in every Australian state and territory.<br /><br />Victoria recorded more than 7000 cases last year [2021] but experts say the real number is likely much higher with many cases not showing symptoms and going undetected.<br /><br />Associate Professor Chow said since 2010, gonorrhoea infections in females had increased more than 5-fold. The number rose from 291 to almost 1600 last year [2021], showing heterosexual gonorrhoea was endemic in Australia.<br /><br />He said lockdowns had not seemed to slow the spread of the infection, particularly in lower socioeconomic areas. \'It\'s just gone up exponentially among women in the outer suburbs of Melbourne,\' Mr Chow said. \'We really don\'t know whether it is because of the lack of sexual health literacy and services, or whether it is more risky behaviour in those areas. But definitely the outer suburbs are becoming our greatest area of concern.\'<br /><br />The Alfred Institute has established 3 general practice clinics in the Melbourne suburbs of Hillside, Tarneit, and Clayton to combat the outbreak.<br /><br />[Byline: Brett Lackey]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED from HealthMap Alerts<br /><br />******<br />[2]<br />Date: Tue 8 Mar 2022 11:55 AEDT<br />Source: The Age [edited]<br /><a href="https://www.theage.com.au/national/gonorrhoea-epidemic-hits-citys-outer-suburbs-20220302-p5a0vv.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.theage.com.au/national/gonorrhoea-epidemic-hits-citys-outer-suburbs-20220302-p5a0vv.html</a><br /><br /><br />Outbreaks of gonorrhoea are spreading rapidly through Melbourne\'s outer suburbs, with doctors warning that the municipalities of Melton, Casey, and Brimbank are now battling an evolving epidemic of the sexually transmitted disease that has alarmed and perplexed experts. New research from Alfred Health has, for the 1st time, tracked the geographical distribution of gonorrhoea over a decade, finding growing clusters of the sexually transmitted infection were infiltrating some of the most socioeconomically disadvantaged areas of Melbourne.<br /><br />Alfred Health epidemiologist and biostatistician Eric Chow, who led the study, said while the disease previously circulated among men who had sex with other men, a growing number of women were becoming infected. "Why this is occurring is the million-dollar question," Associate Professor Chow said. "We really don\'t know whether it is because of the lack of sexual health literacy and services, or whether it is more risky behaviour in those areas. But definitely, the outer suburbs are becoming our greatest area of concern."<br /><br />Victoria recorded more than 7000 gonorrhoea cases last year [2021], compared to roughly 6500 cases in 2020, but screening of people without symptoms plummeted by almost 70 per cent during the pandemic and experts warn the true number of infections is probably far higher than official state government figures.<br /><br />Associate Professor Chow said the study found that since 2010, gonorrhoea infections in females had increased more than 5-fold from 291 in a year, to almost 1600 last year [2021], showing heterosexual gonorrhoea was now endemic in Australia.<br /><br />The research comes as Victoria battles a wave of syphilis outbreaks that has led to at least 4 fetal deaths in Victoria in recent years after several babies contracted syphilis from their mothers. The sharp rise in deaths followed a 14-year absence of fatal cases. Exactly why this is occurring remains unclear. Growing research suggests casual sexual activity reduced and dating app use declined during the pandemic.<br /><br />Associate Professor Chow did say increased sexual promiscuity linked to the explosion in dating apps might have been one factor that had led to a sustained increase in STIs. But he believes the issue is far more complex than that, noting there was a rise in gonorrhoea in the early 2010s, before the online introduction apps became commonplace. "One of the most concerning things to us is the increase in the disease among heterosexual men and women," Associate Professor Chow said. "It\'s just gone up exponentially among women in the outer suburbs of Melbourne."<br /><br />The research found that there was the sharpest rise in cases between 2017 and 2019 with 24 825 notified gonorrhoea cases in Victoria, of which one in 5 were women, 13 per cent were heterosexual males, and about 42 per cent were men who had sex with men. It also found rates of infections of the STI had more than tripled in the outer suburbs of Melbourne.<br /><br />Infections of gonorrhoea among men who have sex with men are concentrated in inner metropolitan Melbourne, and experts said research showed this cohort were the most likely to be regularly screened for STIs, which may explain the higher rates of detection.<br /><br />But of increasing concern to doctors, is the growing number of cases among women concentrated in the outer suburbs, where there remained a worrying lack of health services screening for sexually transmitted diseases and Associate Professor Chow said there was an urgent need for more support.<br /><br />Data from the Victorian government\'s infectious diseases surveillance report shows the City of Yarra, which includes inner-city suburbs Fitzroy, Collingwood, and Abbotsford, had the highest increase in cases, reporting 535 infections last year [2021], compared to 380 in 2020.<br /><br />Problematically, gonorrhoea has become increasingly immune to antibiotics and a drug-resistant strain of the bacteria, dubbed a "super-superbug", has been detected in every Australian state and territory. Associate Professor Chow said there were international concerns about rising resistance to the antibiotic drugs prescribed to treat gonorrhoea. "This is quite concerning because it will make the infection more difficult to treat," he said.<br /><br />Associate Professor Marcus Chen, from Melbourne Sexual Health Centre, said experts were now examining where Victorians were acquiring gonorrhoea, noting a limitation of the recent study was that it was based on the residence of the notified cases. "We\'re getting a feeling there\'s an element of marginalisation linked to outbreaks," Associate Professor Chen said. "There\'s obviously something driving new infections, but if testing and treatment were sufficient to offset it, then you wouldn\'t get a worsening epidemic, which is what we are seeing."<br /><br />[Byline: Melissa Cunningham]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED<br /><br />["Melbourne is the capital and most populous city in the Australian state of Victoria and the 2nd most populous city in Australia." (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melbourne" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melbourne</a>). A ProMED map of Australia can be accessed at <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701917,295" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701917,295</a>.<br /><br />In May 2021, ProMED posted a news report of an outbreak of syphilis in urban poor women in Melbourne\'s outer suburbs (Brimbank and Melton to the city\'s northwest, and Casey, to the city\'s southeast) that was associated with an increase in cases of congenital and ocular syphilis (see ProMED post Syphilis - Australia: (VI) ocular, women, congenital, urban poor, genotyping, alert <a href="javascript:;" onclick="window.open(\'https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=20210518.8367315\');">20210518.8367315</a>). In that outbreak, scientists were said to be using genomic sequencing for the 1st time to track syphilis cases.<br /><br />The May 2021 report attributed the increase in STDs in lower-socio economic communities in Melbourne\'s outer suburbs in part to barriers in accessing healthcare. A report on the effects that social and economic conditions in these areas of Melbourne have on health care can be found in a report entitled "HealthWest Partnership response to the Senate Committees on Community Affairs: Australia\'s domestic response to the World Health Organization\'s (WHO) Commission on Social Determinants of Health report -- Closing the gap within a generation" (<a href="https://bit.ly/3yiFwrI" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://bit.ly/3yiFwrI</a>).<br /><br />The current news reports above are now reporting an outbreak of gonorrhea, another sexually transmitted disease (STD), in the same Melbourne outer suburbs of Brimbank, Melton, and Casey as previously reported for syphilis, among women apparently in the same demographic group that was affected by syphilis. A map showing the location of these 3 Melbourne suburbs can be found at <a href="https://www.theage.com.au/national/gonorrhoea-epidemic-hits-citys-outer-suburbs-20220302-p5a0vv.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.theage.com.au/national/gonorrhoea-epidemic-hits-citys-outer-suburbs-20220302-p5a0vv.html</a>. We are not told if antibiotic resistant strains of gonococci are involved in this outbreak.<br /><br />In recent ProMED posts, illicit drug use, namely methamphetamine, has been cited as a contributing factor to recent increases in STDs in women in both the United States and Canada (see the "See Also" section below). Illicit drug use is associated with sexual behaviors that increase the risk of acquiring syphilis and other sexually transmitted diseases, including having multiple anonymous sex partners, inconsistent condom use, and exchange of sex for drugs or money.<br /><br />More information on this outbreak of STDs in Melbourne suburbs would be appreciated from knowledgeable sources. - This means that these 2 production facilities are now affected. AquaGen stressed that other production facilities have not been affected.\r\n\r\nAquaGen said it has carried out individual screening of all broodstock in their production facilities.\r\n\r\nThe suspicion arose as a result of sampling taken last week [week of 1 Mar 2022] from the broodstock group moved to Kyrksæterøra.\r\n\r\nThe findings have now been reported to the Norwegian Food Safety Authority. It is being stressed that no increased mortality or clinical symptoms have been reported in any of the suspected fish groups.\r\n\r\nThe roe from the broodstock was routinely placed in the quarantine department pending test results, and it is therefore not expected that the suspicion will affect previously produced roe that is in stock at the company.\r\n\r\nAquaGen said the broodstock groups that may have been affected account for up to half of the planned production of salmon roe for deliveries from AquaGen in the 3rd quarter of this year [2022].\r\n\r\nIt adds: "The scope may therefore lead to delays in our roe deliveries planned late in the 2nd quarter and in the 3rd quarter. "\r\n\r\nAquaGen is a breeding company which develops, produces and delivers genetic material to the global aquaculture farming industry and has achieved a leading position as a provider of fertilised eggs of Atlantic salmon and rainbow trout.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Vince McDonagh]\r\n\r\n--\r\ncommunicated by:\r\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\n\n[Infectious salmon anemia (ISA) is a disease of Atlantic salmon (_Salmo salar_) caused by an orthomyxovirus and affects mainly fish maintained in marine water or exposed to the sea. The disease can be systemic and lethal, characterized by severe anemia and hemorrhages in several organs.\r\n\r\nIt is a disease of great economic impact for the salmon industry. Norway: (MR) susp <br /><span class="blue">Archive Number:</span> 20220310.8701916<div class="text1">INFECTIOUS SALMON ANEMIA - NORWAY: (MØRE OG ROMSDAL) SUSPECTED<br />***************************************************************<br />A ProMED-mail post<br /><a href="http://www.promedmail.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.promedmail.org</a><br />ProMED-mail is a program of the<br />International Society for Infectious Diseases<br /><a href="http://www.isid.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.isid.org</a><br /><br />Date: Wed 9 Mar 2022<br />Source: Fish Farmer [edited]<br /><a href="https://www.fishfarmermagazine.com/news/isa-outbreak-feared-at-aquagen-sites/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.fishfarmermagazine.com/news/isa-outbreak-feared-at-aquagen-sites/</a><br /><br /><br />Norway has reported its 1st suspected case of infectious salmon anaemia (ISA) in several weeks, at a broodstock group at the AquaGen sites at Ørsta and Heim in the west of the country [Møre og Romsdal county].<br /><br />The company said in a press release that parts of this group of broodstock have been transported to AquaGen\'s land facility at Kyrksæterøra in Heim.<br /><br />The transport was made before suspicions arose. This means that these 2 production facilities are now affected. AquaGen stressed that other production facilities have not been affected.<br /><br />AquaGen said it has carried out individual screening of all broodstock in their production facilities.<br /><br />The suspicion arose as a result of sampling taken last week [week of 1 Mar 2022] from the broodstock group moved to Kyrksæterøra.<br /><br />The findings have now been reported to the Norwegian Food Safety Authority. It is being stressed that no increased mortality or clinical symptoms have been reported in any of the suspected fish groups.<br /><br />The roe from the broodstock was routinely placed in the quarantine department pending test results, and it is therefore not expected that the suspicion will affect previously produced roe that is in stock at the company.<br /><br />AquaGen said the broodstock groups that may have been affected account for up to half of the planned production of salmon roe for deliveries from AquaGen in the 3rd quarter of this year [2022].<br /><br />It adds: "The scope may therefore lead to delays in our roe deliveries planned late in the 2nd quarter and in the 3rd quarter. "<br /><br />AquaGen is a breeding company which develops, produces and delivers genetic material to the global aquaculture farming industry and has achieved a leading position as a provider of fertilised eggs of Atlantic salmon and rainbow trout.<br /><br />[Byline: Vince McDonagh]<br /><br />--<br />communicated by:<br />ProMED from HealthMap Alerts<br /><br />[Infectious salmon anemia (ISA) is a disease of Atlantic salmon (_Salmo salar_) caused by an orthomyxovirus and affects mainly fish maintained in marine water or exposed to the sea. The disease can be systemic and lethal, characterized by severe anemia and hemorrhages in several organs.<br /><br />It is a disease of great economic impact for the salmon industry. The disease is of obligatory notification to the OIE. - Mod.PMB<br /><br />ProMED map:<br />Ørsta, Møre og Romsdal, Norway: <a href="https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701916,68688" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701916,68688</a>] <h2>See Also</h2>\n2019<br />----<br />Infectious salmon anemia - Data as reported by: 17:00; 6 Mar 2022\r\n--------------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\nThe Central African Republic recorded 4 cases of monkeypox, including 2 deaths, during epidemiological week 8 [week ending 26 Feb 2022], in the health districts of Mbaïki and Bimbo. The epidemiological investigation is ongoing.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nMary Marshall\r\n<mjm2020@googlemail.com>\n\n[This very brief report indicates that there have been 4 monkeypox cases reported in the Central African Republic (CAR) so far this year (2022), of which 2 died of the disease.\r\n\r\nProMED has reported sporadic cases of monkeypox (MPX) in the Central African Republic (CAR). Since 2013, except for 2020 and 2021, CAR has been reporting at least one MPX outbreak every year, especially in its eastern region. The case fatality rate continues to be very low except for the 2 deaths of 4 cases reported above. However, these are very small numbers and do not provide reliable case fatality rates.\r\n\r\nPrevention of MPX virus infections will not be possible without knowing the source of infection. The question remains about the source of these recent infections within the CAR as well as in Nigeria, Cameroon, and Liberia. Monkeys are not the reservoirs of the virus, despite the name that the virus has received.\r\n\r\nStudies of prevalence of MPX virus in populations of rodent hosts are not mentioned in this or previous reports. The main reservoirs of MPX virus are suspected to be rodents, including rope squirrels (_Funisciurus_ spp., an arboreal rodent) and terrestrial rodents in the genera _Cricetomys_ and _Graphiurus_. Halting the bushmeat trade and consumption of wild animals to halt MPX virus exposure will be culturally and economically difficult, so continued occurrence of cases can be expected.\r\n\r\nThe MPX virus clade involved in this outbreak and previous ones in the CAR is not mentioned. As noted in previous ProMED posts, the monkeypox virus clade in the Congo Basin causes more severe disease in humans -- with a case fatality rate of up to17 percent -- than the clade in Ghana, which causes few fatalities. - Mod.TY\n\nProMED map:\nCentral African Republic: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701910,66>]\n\n[See Also:\n2019\r\n----\r\nMonkeypox - Africa: Central African Republic 20190205.6299251\r\n2018\r\n----\r\nMonkeypox - The epidemiological investigation is ongoing.<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />Mary Marshall<br />&lt;mjm2020@googlemail.com><br /><br />[This very brief report indicates that there have been 4 monkeypox cases reported in the Central African Republic (CAR) so far this year (2022), of which 2 died of the disease.<br /><br />ProMED has reported sporadic cases of monkeypox (MPX) in the Central African Republic (CAR). Since 2013, except for 2020 and 2021, CAR has been reporting at least one MPX outbreak every year, especially in its eastern region. The case fatality rate continues to be very low except for the 2 deaths of 4 cases reported above. However, these are very small numbers and do not provide reliable case fatality rates.<br /><br />Prevention of MPX virus infections will not be possible without knowing the source of infection. The question remains about the source of these recent infections within the CAR as well as in Nigeria, Cameroon, and Liberia. Monkeys are not the reservoirs of the virus, despite the name that the virus has received.<br /><br />Studies of prevalence of MPX virus in populations of rodent hosts are not mentioned in this or previous reports. The main reservoirs of MPX virus are suspected to be rodents, including rope squirrels (_Funisciurus_ spp., an arboreal rodent) and terrestrial rodents in the genera _Cricetomys_ and _Graphiurus_. Halting the bushmeat trade and consumption of wild animals to halt MPX virus exposure will be culturally and economically difficult, so continued occurrence of cases can be expected.<br /><br />The MPX virus clade involved in this outbreak and previous ones in the CAR is not mentioned. Greene County in central Iowa and Fremont County in southwest Iowa brings the total number of counties to 12.\r\n\r\nCWD was first detected in Iowa in 2013 with 72 cases in Allamakee County in northeast Iowa, the most cases in any one county in any year since. The 2nd most were 29 CWD cases in neighboring Clayton County in 2016. Ten cases were detected in Winneshiek County and 2 in Fayette County in 2019.\r\n\r\nHarms says, overall for the state there\'s been a 2% prevalence rate of CWD out of the 5000 samples, which is about what the DNR expected. He adds the goal is to keep that prevalence as low as possible.\r\n\r\nHarms encourages deer hunters to keep hunting and keep submitting samples for testing and to properly dispose of the deer carcasses to help prevent the spread of the disease. He adds that the general public can also help by not putting out feed for deer, noting that CWD is spread via direct contact between individual animals.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Mark Pitz]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[ProMED map of Iowa, United States: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701909,218>]\r\n\r\n******\r\n[2] Mississippi (Warren County): deer\r\nDate: Sun 2 Jan 2022\r\nSource: Magnolia State Live [edited]\r\n<https://www.magnoliastatelive.com/2022/01/02/deer-found-in-mississippi-tests-positive-for-chronic-wasting-disease/>\r\n\r\n\r\nA deer found in Warren County has tested positive for chronic wasting disease, the Mississippi Department of Wildlife, Fisheries, and Parks [MDWFP] announced Thursday [30 Dec 2021].\r\n\r\nThe mature buck was reported to MDWFP in mid-December [2021] as potentially diseased given its drastically emaciated and lethargic condition. It was found approximately 4 mi [6.4 km] north of Vicksburg and 4.5 mi [7.2 km] south of where the 1st CWD-positive white-tailed deer was detected in Mississippi, in Issaquena County, in 2018.\r\n\r\nThe sample is considered "suspect positive" through initial testing and will be sent to the National Veterinary Services Laboratory in Ames, Iowa, for final confirmation.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Ben Hillyer]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[There appears now to be a 2nd CWD case in Warren County as of 1 Feb 2022. To view the article please see <https://www.vicksburgpost.com/2022/02/01/lab-confirms-case-of-chronic-wasting-disease-in-warren-county-deer/>. Chronic wasting disease seems relatively abundant, and it has been ProMED\'s policy to post the 1st incident within a county. - Mod.TG\r\n\r\nProMED map of Warren County, Mississippi, United States: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701909,33851>]\r\n\r\n******\r\n[3] Wisconsin (Waukesha County): deer (farmed)\r\nDate: Thu 10 Feb 2022\r\nSource: TMJ4 [edited]\r\n<https://www.tmj4.com/news/local-news/two-deers-in-waukesha-county-test-positive-for-contagious-chronic-wasting-disease>\r\n\r\n\r\nTwo white-tailed deer in Waukesha County have tested positive for chronic wasting disease (CWD), according to the Wisconsin Department of Agriculture. The farm they were raised in is under quarantine.\r\n\r\nCWD is a neurological disease caused by an infection. It can be contagious, which is why the 9-acre farm is being quarantined. Farm-raised deer are generally used for their antlers, venison, pelts, and more.\r\n\r\nCWD is normally tested in animals after they have already died.\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\r\n\r\n[ProMED map of Waukesha County, Wisconsin, United States: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701909,11881>]\r\n\r\n******\r\n[4] Virginia (Floyd County): deer\r\nDate: Tue 8 Mar 2022\r\nSource: WSLS [edited]\r\n<https://www.wsls.com/news/local/2022/03/08/first-ever-floyd-county-deer-tests-positive-for-chronic-wasting-disease/>\r\n\r\n\r\nWildlife officials are alerting people to a diseased deer killed in Floyd County this hunting season.\r\n\r\nOn Tuesday [8 Mar 2022], the Virginia Department of Wildlife Resources released its chronic wasting disease surveillance results for the 2021-2022 hunting season. In Virginia, a total of 134 deer from 11 counties have tested positive for the disease since 2009.\r\n\r\nThis incurable disease, found in deer, elk, and moose in North America, is a slow and progressive neurologic disease ultimately resulting in death of the animal. The disease-causing agent is spread through the urine, feces, and saliva of infected animals.\r\n\r\nIn CWD Disease Management (DMA) Area 3, which comprises Floyd, Montgomery, and Pulaski counties, of the 1259 deer tested, 2 tested positive for the disease: one in Montgomery County and the other in Floyd County.\r\n\r\nA 3rd deer, sampled by a cooperator located in DMA3, was determined to be infected with CWD; however, the location of harvest for this animal was not able to be confirmed.\r\n\r\nBecause of the new CWD detection in Floyd County, the Department of Wildlife Resources is expanding that DMA to include Carroll County.\r\n\r\nOfficials said the diseased deer found in Floyd County was about 5 mi [8 km] from the 2020 Montgomery County detection, and less than 10 mi [16 km] from Carroll County.\r\n\r\n[Byline: Jeff Williamson]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED from HealthMap Alerts\r\n\r\n[ProMED map of Floyd County, Virginia, United States: <https://promedmail.org/promed-post?place=8701909,22874>]\n\n["Chronic wasting disease (CWD) is a fatal, neurological illness occurring in North American cervids (members of the deer family), including white-tailed deer, mule deer, elk, and moose. Since its discovery in 1967, CWD has spread geographically and increased in prevalence locally. CWD is contagious; it can be transmitted freely within and among cervid populations. No treatments or vaccines are currently available.\r\n\r\n"Chronic wasting disease is of great concern to wildlife managers. It has been detected in at least 23 states, 2 Canadian provinces, and South Korea. CWD is not known to infect livestock or humans.\r\n\r\n"CWD is transmitted directly through animal-to-animal contact, and indirectly through contact with objects or environment contaminated with infectious material (including saliva, urine, feces, and carcasses of CWD-infected animals)."\r\n(<https://www.usgs.gov/faqs/what-chronic-wasting-disease>) - Since its discovery in 1967, CWD has spread geographically and increased in prevalence locally. CWD is contagious; it can be transmitted freely within and among cervid populations. No treatments or vaccines are currently available.<br /><br />"Chronic wasting disease is of great concern to wildlife managers. It has been detected in at least 23 states, 2 Canadian provinces, and South Korea. CWD is not known to infect livestock or humans.<br /><br />"CWD is transmitted directly through animal-to-animal contact, and indirectly through contact with objects or environment contaminated with infectious material (including saliva, urine, feces, and carcasses of CWD-infected animals)."<br />(<a href="https://www.usgs.gov/faqs/what-chronic-wasting-disease" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://www.usgs.gov/faqs/what-chronic-wasting-disease</a>) - Mod.DHA, edited]\r\n<https://dfnet.fftc.org.tw/Page/ArticleDetail.aspx?ArticleID=ou9dT%2Fy%2B3RU%3D&PI=8ttmTAm9Tdg%3D&Co=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Ca=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Ws=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Keyword=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D>\r\n\r\n\r\nA new destructive disease called stem canker was reported in dragon fruit (_Hylocereus polyrhizus_) in Bangladesh [see link below], which forced some farmers to abandon cultivation. The disease has spread since then. In 2019, it had been associated with _Lasiodiplodia_ sp. based mainly on morphology, with _Hylocereus_ as a new host for this genus. A molecular study had to be carried out to confirm the causal agent to species level, as well as determine its phylogeny, epidemiology, and host range.\r\n\r\nOf 8 fungal isolates from symptomatic dragon fruit stems, 2 were analysed by morphology, as well as phylogeny of sequence data from 3 different genomic regions. They were identified as _Lasiodiplodia theobromae_. Inoculation trials on dragon fruit stems confirmed Koch's postulate. The isolates were also found pathogenic on mango, guava, banana, and _H. polyrhizus_ fruits.\r\n\r\nThe data will contribute to understanding the biology of _L. theobromae_ as a newly recognised pathogen of dragon fruit, as well as help to design effective management strategies against this pathogen.\r\n\r\n[Source publication: <https://doi.org/10.1002/jobm.202100501> or <https://bit.ly/3MEKZjC>]\r\n\r\n--\r\nCommunicated by:\r\nProMED\n\n[Dragon fruit (also called pitaya, strawberry pear) is the common name for several cactus species and hybrids, mostly of the genus _Hylocereus_, but also _Stenocereus_ and some other related genera. These vine-like epiphytic cacti originate in Central and South America but are also widely grown in Southeast Asia. They are an important fruit crop in these regions because of their high nutritional value. Several varieties with varying skin and pulp colours are planted commercially. Few pathogens are known to affect the crops, but disease management is especially difficult since dragon fruit is propagated by cuttings, which may spread any pathogens.\r\n\r\nThe fungus _Lasiodiplodia theobromae_ was first reported in Cameroon in 1895 associated with charcoal pod rot of cocoa. Subsequently it was found to have a wide host range of more than 280 species including many crops such as citrus, grapevine, vegetable hosts, strawberry, sweet potato, and mango. Depending on the host, symptoms may include wilting, fruit rots, dieback, vascular discolouration, complete defoliation, and death of plants. It is thought that nutrient deficiencies and environmental stress factors may enhance the susceptibility of some hosts. Fungicides may be helpful in disease management if applied quickly enough. An increase in virulence has been reported on some hosts, suggesting that new strains of the fungus may be emerging in different areas.\r\n\r\nMaps\r\nBangladesh:\r\n<http://www.nationsonline.org/maps/bangladesh_map.jpg> and\r\n<http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-OvthAOOs_tE/T6qxrewlF8I/AAAAAAAAAKw/Qg1nYXeyA9A/s1600/BangladeshDistrictsMap.JPG>\r\n\r\nPictures\r\n_L. theobromae_ symptoms on different Mod.DHA, edited]<br /><a href="https://dfnet.fftc.org.tw/Page/ArticleDetail.aspx?ArticleID=ou9dT%2Fy%2B3RU%3D&PI=8ttmTAm9Tdg%3D&Co=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Ca=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Ws=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Keyword=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://dfnet.fftc.org.tw/Page/ArticleDetail.aspx?ArticleID=ou9dT%2Fy%2B3RU%3D&PI=8ttmTAm9Tdg%3D&Co=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Ca=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Ws=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D&Keyword=ztBzV%2F10sco%3D</a><br /><br /><br />A new destructive disease called stem canker was reported in dragon fruit (_Hylocereus polyrhizus_) in Bangladesh [see link below], which forced some farmers to abandon cultivation. The disease has spread since then. In 2019, it had been associated with _Lasiodiplodia_ sp. based mainly on morphology, with _Hylocereus_ as a new host for this genus. A molecular study had to be carried out to confirm the causal agent to species level, as well as determine its phylogeny, epidemiology, and host range.<br /><br />Of 8 fungal isolates from symptomatic dragon fruit stems, 2 were analysed by morphology, as well as phylogeny of sequence data from 3 different genomic regions. They were identified as _Lasiodiplodia theobromae_. Inoculation trials on dragon fruit stems confirmed Koch\'s postulate. The isolates were also found pathogenic on mango, guava, banana, and _H. polyrhizus_ fruits.<br /><br />The data will contribute to understanding the biology of _L. theobromae_ as a newly recognised pathogen of dragon fruit, as well as help to design effective management strategies against this pathogen.<br /><br />[Source publication: <a href="https://doi.org/10.1002/jobm.202100501" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://doi.org/10.1002/jobm.202100501</a> or <a href="https://bit.ly/3MEKZjC" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://bit.ly/3MEKZjC</a>]<br /><br />--<br />Communicated by:<br />ProMED<br /><br />[Dragon fruit (also called pitaya, strawberry pear) is the common name for several cactus species and hybrids, mostly of the genus _Hylocereus_, but also _Stenocereus_ and some other related genera. These vine-like epiphytic cacti originate in Central and South America but are also widely grown in Southeast Asia. They are an important fruit crop in these regions because of their high nutritional value. Several varieties with varying skin and pulp colours are planted commercially. Few pathogens are known to affect the crops, but disease management is especially difficult since dragon fruit is propagated by cuttings, which may spread any pathogens.<br /><br />The fungus _Lasiodiplodia theobromae_ was first reported in Cameroon in 1895 associated with charcoal pod rot of cocoa. Subsequently it was found to have a wide host range of more than 280 species including many crops such as citrus, grapevine, vegetable hosts, strawberry, sweet potato, and mango. Depending on the host, symptoms may include wilting, fruit rots, dieback, vascular discolouration, complete defoliation, and death of plants. It is thought that nutrient deficiencies and environmental stress factors may enhance the susceptibility of some hosts. Fungicides may be helpful in disease management if applied quickly enough. An increase in virulence has been reported on some hosts, suggesting that new strains of the fungus may be emerging in different areas.<br /><br />Maps<br />Bangladesh:<br /><a
